{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","updatedTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","title":"7 books that can supercharge your personal growth this summer","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/books-to-read-to-supercharge-personal-growth-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/605ddddf6746fb0018a73dde?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman reading book bed\" height=\"1013\" width=\"1351\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Feeling burned out and jaded? Invest some time and energy into your personal growth.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dougal Waters/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The following article was first published by <a href=\"https://nextbigideaclub.com/\">The Next Big Idea Club</a> and has been republished here with permission.</li>\n<li>Diving into an impactful book is a great way to kick off a journey of personal growth.</li>\n<li>if you&#39;d like to invest some time and energy into personal growth, these 7 books are an excellent place to start.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Over the last year, many of us have felt the world spin out of control. The global pandemic has forced us to abandon familiar routines and adopt new habits for everything, from working to socializing.</p><p>But no matter what the pandemic puts us through, there&#39;s one thing we can always control: ourselves. So if you&#39;d like to invest some time and energy into personal growth, the seven books below are an excellent place to start.</p><h2>1. &#34;The Power of Ritual: Turning Everyday Activities into Soulful Practices&#34; by Casper ter Kuile</h2><p>In America and around the world, it&#39;s no secret that many people are struggling to find fulfillment in traditional organized religion. But Harvard Divinity School Fellow Casper ter Kuile believes that whether you&#39;re religious or not, you can design personal rituals for your life, rituals that add joy and meaning to everyday experiences. </p><p><em><a href=\"https://nextbigidea.app.link/ter-Kuile\">View Our &#34;Book Bite&#34; Summary</a></em></p><figure></figure><h2>2. &#34;In Awe: Rediscover Your Childlike Wonder to Unleash Inspiration, Meaning, and Joy&#34; by John O&#39;Leary</h2><p>With so much bad news showing up everywhere from TV to Twitter, we may find ourselves feeling burned out and jaded more often than we&#39;d like. But internationally renowned speaker John O&#39;Leary believes that we can adopt a different, healthier, more joyful mindset - if only we&#39;re ready to try a new perspective.  </p><p><em><a href=\"https://nextbigideaclub.com/magazine/awe-rediscover-childlike-wonder-unleash-inspiration-meaning-joy-bookbite/25303/\">View Our &#34;Book Bite&#34; Summary</a></em></p><h2>3. &#34;Think Like a Monk: Train Your Mind for Peace and Purpose Every Day&#34; by Jay Shetty</h2><p>When business and media influencer Jay Shetty encourages us to &#34;think like a monk,&#34; he&#39;s not referencing something he read about, or researched for a doctorate degree. He&#39;s talking about something he <em>lived</em>, as he spent years in India as a monk himself. This remarkable book lays bare the most ancient, most valuable wisdom he learned along the way.</p><p><em> <a href=\"https://nextbigidea.app.link/Shetty\">View Our &#34;Book Bite&#34; Summary</a></em></p><h2>4. &#34;Bravey: Chasing Dreams, Befriending Pain, and Other Big Ideas&#34; by Alexi Pappas</h2><p>Olympic athlete, actress, and filmmaker Alexi Pappas may seem to have it all figured out. But when she was just four years old, her mother died by suicide - and over the years, she&#39;s had to battle demons of her own. In this candid and moving memoir, Pappas shares what she&#39;s learned about overcoming adversity and living the life you&#39;ve always wanted.</p><p><em><a href=\"https://nextbigidea.app.link/Pappas\">View Our &#34;Book Bite&#34; Summary</a></em></p><h2>5. &#34;Being the Person Your Dog Thinks You Are: The Science of a Better You&#34; by Jim Davies</h2><p>Your dog thinks you&#39;re probably the best person in the world. After all, enduring your absence for even half an hour seems to stress her out. So if you want to become every bit as kind, generous, and wise as she thinks you are, you&#39;ll want to crack open this book by cognitive scientist Jim Davies. </p><p><em><a href=\"https://nextbigidea.app.link/Davies\">View Our &#34;Book Bite&#34; Summary</a></em></p><h2>6. &#34;The Socrates Express: In Search of Life Lessons from Dead Philosophers&#34; by Eric Weiner</h2><p>Wondering about how to attain true happiness, or how to become a more ethical person, or what the meaning of life could be? If so, there&#39;s no need to start answering those questions from scratch - in fact, history&#39;s greatest minds have already done the heavy lifting. Let Eric Weiner be your guide through their greatest insights. </p><p><em><a href=\"https://nextbigidea.app.link/Weiner\">View Our &#34;Book Bite&#34; Summary</a></em></p><h2>7. &#34;Beginners: The Joy and Transformative Power of Lifelong Learning&#34; by Tom Vanderbilt</h2><p>When we&#39;re kids, we constantly try new hobbies, sports, and activities. And although we&#39;re not always successful, these forays help us become stronger, more well-rounded individuals. So why do we stop trying new things in adulthood? In &#34;Beginners,&#34; acclaimed journalist Tom Vanderbilt contends that you&#39;re never too old to learn something new. </p><p><em><a href=\"https://nextbigidea.app.link/Vanderbilt\">View Our &#34;Book Bite&#34; Summary</a></em></p><p><strong><em>Read more:</em></strong></p><p><em><a Mike Lindell at the White House.\n<p class=\"copyright\">MANDEL NGAN/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>MyPillow CEO Mike Lindell said Fox News hadn&#39;t covered his upcoming &#34;cyber symposium&#34; event.</li>\n<li>He told <a time on the network, <a href=\"https://www.salon.com/2021/07/23/mike-lindell-angry-that-fox-news-is-ignoring-his-cyber-symposium-on-election-fraud/\">Salon</a> reports. </p><p>Lindell said the news network hadn&#39;t yet covered his <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/my-pillow-mike-lindell-offers-5-million-disprove-voter-fraud-2021-7\">&#34;cyber symposium&#34;</a> event, scheduled to start August 10 in South Dakota. </p><p>&#34;Fox [News] does not talk about anything with the election,&#34; he told Salon. Fox News did not immediately respond to Insider&#39;s request for comment. </p><p>Lindell said he planned to respond by buying more ads on Fox News. Those ads would promote his website, <a href=\"https://frankspeech.com/\">FrankSpeech.com,</a> and include information about the event in an attempt to &#34;get the word out,&#34; he said. </p><p>&#34;So I&#39;m going to make ads that will talk about - at least advertising for FrankSpeech.com - that we&#39;re going to be televising this [cyber symposium] for 72 hours straight,&#34; he said. </p><p>Lindell has said his symposium would reveal new information about voter fraud in the 2020 election. An ally of former President Donald Trump, he has been a leading voice in spreading conspiracies theories about the election being <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-mypillow-ceo-mike-lindell-election-fraud-claims-voting-2021-2\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"335770bef39fa100cc7c4ca9c39c5e11\">&#34;stolen.&#34;</a> </p><p>In December 2020, Lindell <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/video-sebastian-gorka-shuts-down-mypillow-ceo-mike-lindell-newsmax-2020-12\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"a9e6f56a3e027565ea1b478738b683c3\">said</a> &#34;the biggest fraud is the Dominion machines,&#34; a reference to machines used to cast votes. He said Dominion&#39;s technology <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-sidney-powell-libel-billion-damages-2021-1\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"6803ff7ac352c32afe4b343ae2530a53\">switched</a> votes for Trump to votes for Joe Biden. Dominion <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-mypillow-ceo-mike-lindell-election-fraud-claims-voting-2021-2\">sued</a> Lindell for $1.3 billion, and Lindell <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mike-lindell-mypillow-dominion-lawsuit-trump-voter-fraud-2021-4\">countered</a> with a lawsuit for $1.6 billion.</p><p>Lindell told Salon: &#34;Fox News has refused to cover election fraud, especially the machines.&#34; He added: &#34;Shame on Fox News!&#34; </p><p>Following the 2020 elections, Lindell&#39;s relationship with Fox News soured. He said the network was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-calls-fox-news-unwatchable-criticism-newsmax-2020-11\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"f3ccee07373b3a9ed8ecfe01c2bffec4\">&#34;unwatchable&#34;</a> after it announced Biden&#39;s victory. He championed other conservative networks, like Newsmax.</p><p>Lindell went after the network on Steve Bannon&#39;s<a href=\"https://americasvoice.news/playlists/the-war-room/?currentPage=3\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"4b560142382906bebdbb73806460c008\"> podcast &#34;War Room: Pandemic&#34; on Real America&#39;s Voice.</a> He told Bannon that MSNBC has way &#34;better coverage&#34;  than Fox News. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Images/Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A Bay Area family left a Southwest Airlines flight over a mask incident. </li>\n<li>The family said they felt pressured to leave when their toddler could not keep his mask on. </li>\n<li>They are vowing to never fly on Southwest Airlines again, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A California family said Southwest Airlines &#34;just wanted them off the plane&#34; when their 3-year-old son refused to keep his face mask on. </p><p>After the experience, the family is vowing to never fly on the airline again.</p><p>Eric Hansen, his wife, and their toddler were all ready to fly from Las Vegas to San Jose on Friday 23 July, <a href=\"https://www.kron4.com/news/bay-area/bay-area-family-leaves-southwest-flight-after-confrontation-over-3-year-old-not-wearing-mask/\">KRON4 reported</a>.</p><p>&#34;They&#39;re a pretty big airline in the Bay Area but I am going to do all I can to not get another one of their flights and potentially go through another situation like this,&#34; Hansen told KRON4. </p><p>Hansen said two flight attendants and a gate agent treated them like criminals. When they feared police were being called to arrest them, they voluntarily stepped off the flight, according to KRON4.</p><p>The family said they had to spend an extra night in Las Vegas without any of their checked baggage, as a result. </p><p>&#34;They should have given us more time, maybe walked away and said we will give you five or 10 minutes, but their flight was late so I think they were trying to make time. They just wanted us off the plane and they didn&#39;t give us any time to talk him through it and try to get him to put it on,&#34; Hansen said. </p><p>Hansen complained to the airline, which sent him an email apologizing for his experience on the flight. But it also stated that under the CDC&#39;s &#34;Federal mask mandate, all customers (age 2 or over) are required to wear a mask. If the customer does not comply with crew member instructions, we may refuse transportation.&#34; </p><p>Southwest Airlines did not immediately respond to Insider&#39;s request for comment</p><p>Hansen told KRON4 that the policy was inconsistent because his son was maskless on the inbound flight to Las Vegas and the rebooked Southwest flight back to San Jose the next day. </p><p>In a similar incident in April, a family of three were <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/family-kicked-off-southwest-airlines-free-private-flight-austin-texas-2021-4\">booted off a Southwest Airlines</a> flight after their 2-year-old could not keep his mask on. </p><p>In that case, a passenger named Erik Harvey, his wife Michelle, and their toddler Jackson were all ready to fly from Denver to Austin on April 1, <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/us/southwest-passengers-booted-over-mask-dispute-get-a-lift-from-small-plane-pilot\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"b7227148c346aebf7a9b104f70477166\">Fox News reported. </a>However, they were told to leave because Jackson was unmasked.</p><p>A Good Samaritan later 18:54:06","updatedTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","title":"You won't go to space any time soon, no matter what the billionaires say","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/space-tourism-you-wont-go-to-space-any-time-soon-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60cf17c8db3f80001848cd97?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Elon Musk, Jeff Bezos, Richard Branson\" height=\"2249\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Elon Musk, Jeff Bezos, Richard Branson\n<p class=\"copyright\">Patrick Pluel/Getty Images; Alex Wong/Getty Images; Hollis Johnson/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>This month, billionaires Jeff Bezos and Richard Branson went on suborbital space flights with their respective companies. </li>\n<li>The billionaires say they plan to make space tourism mainstream, but the trips came with hefty price tags.</li>\n<li>Space law experts say the prices aren&#39;t the only thing that will stop the average person from going on a space tour.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Billionaires Jeff Bezos and Richard Branson have drawn public attention to space tourism after they traveled to the edge of space this month, but it&#39;s unlikely the average person will get to visit space in the foreseeable future.</p><p>It is likely that space tourism will be a hobby solely reserved for billionaires and centi-millionaires for many years to come. </p><p>Ticket prices for suborbital tours on Branson&#39;s Virgin Galactic are selling for around <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/celebrities-reserve-tickets-to-fly-space-richard-branson-virgin-galactic-2021-7\">$250,000 per person.</a> To date, about <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/celebrities-reserve-tickets-to-fly-space-richard-branson-virgin-galactic-2021-7\">600 people have reserved tickets</a> to fly with the company to the edge of space.</p><p>While Bezos&#39; Blue Origin has yet to release its ticket prices, the Amazon founder has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jeff-bezos-blue-origin-to-sell-tickets-space-tourism-rocket-2021-4\">indicated</a> that the tickets will be competitive with Branson&#39;s company. The first available ticket on Bezos&#39; flight sold for $28 million at auction and the entire 10 minute trip on Tuesday <a href=\"https://fortune.com/2021/07/19/jeff-bezos-space-launch-blue-origin-july-20-2021-billionaires/\">cost the billionaire about $5.5 billion</a> out-of-pocket. The same day, the company said it had <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2021/07/20/jeff-bezos-blue-origin-space-tourist-sales-approaching-100-million.html\">sold about $100 million worth of tickets</a> for future passengers to ride on the 4-person aircraft.</p><p>Bezos said he plans to launch future flights at a &#34;very high&#34; rate going forward. &#34;We need to get as good at running space tours as we are as a civilization at running commercial airliners,&#34; he said.</p><p>SpaceX CEO Elon Musk has said that <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2016/9/27/13078690/elon-musk-mars-mission-cost-per-person-spacex\">he believes</a> the cost of going to space, in particular visiting Mars (a trip that would <a href=\"https://www.mars-one.com/faq/finance-and-feasibility/what-is-mars-ones-mission-budget\">cost about $10 billion per person</a> using current technology), will one day be equivalent to the cost of buying a house.</p><p>But, the truth is current technology is too expensive for the average person to be able to afford a seat on one of Bezos, Branson or Musk&#39;s rockets. Though Bezos and Musk have been progressively working to make space travel more affordable through th<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/in-space-missions-spacex-satellite-space-rocket-2021-7\">e development of reusable rockets</a>, the industry is still in its beginning stages.</p><p>Space law experts told Insider that even outside of the sheer cost of space tourism there are several hurdles the companies must overcome before space tourism can become a viable industry for everyday people. These include creating standard regulations akin to the policies that guard airplanes, as well as developing strategies to better <a href=\"https://www.axios.com/air-traffic-control-space-launch-72169cc4-f879-4cbf-8028-71c55208fded.html\">manage air travel</a> and <a href=\"https://www.independent.co.uk/climate-change/news/bezos-rocket-carbon-emissions-blue-origin-b1888059.html\">pollution</a> from the flights.</p><p>People who ride with Blue Origin or Virgin Galactic &#34;are not astronauts or passengers, legally speaking,&#34; the director of McGill&#39;s Institute of Air and Space Law, <a href=\"https://www.mcgill.ca/law/about/profs/jakhu-ram\">Ram Jakhu</a> told Insider. &#34;They are called spaceflight participants, which means they are essentially people participating in an experiment with a massive risk.&#34;</p><p>As it stands, individuals that currently purchase space tourism tickets must sign an <a href=\"https://research-compliance.umich.edu/informed-consent-guidelines\">informed consent document</a> releasing companies from liability if the ticket-holders are injured or killed.</p><p>Spokespeople from Blue Origin and Virgin Galactic did not respond to a request for comment, but Jakhu and <a href=\"https://law.unl.edu/frans-von-der-dunk/\">Frans Von der Dunk</a>, a professor of Space Law at University of Nebraska-Lincoln told Insider the risk would likely deter the general public, even if the hefty price tag had not already narrowed the field of participants.</p><p>What&#39;s more the flights themselves would also have to be more persuasive for tourists. </p><p>&#34;Right now, these flights are just a sophisticated form of bungee jumping,&#34; Von der Dunk said. </p><p>On Tuesday, one of Blue Origin&#39;s flight participants, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jeff-bezos-guest-wally-funk-describes-dark-short-crowded-spaceflight-2021-7\">Wally Funk, expressed discontent with the trip, </a>saying it was crowded.</p><p>&#34;I thought I was going to see the world, but we weren&#39;t quite high enough,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jeff-bezos-guest-wally-funk-describes-dark-short-crowded-spaceflight-2021-7\">Funk said in a presser after the flight.</a></p><p>Branson&#39;s flight received <a href=\"https://www.foxbusiness.com/technology/virgin-galactic-flubs-livestream-branson-spaceflight\">similar criticism</a> after the Virgin Galactic flight only went 85 kilometers high, slightly lower than Bezos&#39; flight.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/space-tourism-you-wont-go-to-space-any-time-soon-2021-7'>Business like it before,&#34; Patrick Maney, who also was on the plane, told NOLA.</p><p>He added: &#34;Two heavily armed police came and told the lady to get off. She refused, and they then told her to get up. She was screaming and resisting as they hauled her up and put some kind of restraints on her hands behind her back.&#34;</p><p>American Airlines did not immediately respond to Insider&#39;s request for comment. </p><p>The passenger was arrested at around 10 a.m CST, Captain Jason Rivarde, a spokesperson for Jefferson Parish Sheriff&#39;s Office, told Nola.</p><p>According to the outlet, officials said the passenger was ticketed for four misdemeanors: disturbing the peace, remaining in a place after being forbidden, resisting arrest, and simple assault.</p><p>It follows a series of mask-related incidents on planes at a time when <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/violence-on-airplanes-in-stores-explained-harvard-psychologist-2021-7?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">violence is spiking</a>.</p><p>Most recently, a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/southwest-airlines-flight-california-maskless-toddler-bay-area-2021-7\">California family</a> had to leave a Southwest Airlines flight after their toddler could not keep his face mask on, as Insider reported..</p><p>The family is vowing to never fly on the airline again after the airline crew treated them like criminals because of their maskless child.</p><p>In June, an American Airlines flight had to be canceled Monday after a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/american-airlines-flight-cancelled-after-teens-refuse-to-wear-masks-2021-7\">group of high school students refused to wear mask</a>s. As a result of the incident, the flight had to be delayed overnight and passengers had to stay in airport hotels.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 18:54:06","updatedTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","title":"Chipotle's stores had their most profitable quarter since since 2015 despite the chain raising src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cc1ca30daa9a93d390b06b5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Chipotle\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption> \n   <p class=\"copyright\">Hollis Johnson/Business Insider</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\"> \n <li>Chipotle just announced high restaurant operating margins from the second quarter of 2021.</li> \n <li>Margins were up despite the chain raising wages this summer.</li> \n <li>Chipotle says raising menu prices led to the increased profitability.</li> \n <li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider's business page</a>.</li> \n</ul>\n<p>Chipotle just had a hugely successful quarter, with its most profitable period for its stores since 2015 after raising wages for workers.</p>\n<p>The chain posted that restaurant-level operating margins, which is the amount of revenue stores took in after factoring in costs for ingredients, labor, and other expenses, was 24.5% for the second quarter of 2021. The higher the margin, the more profitable the period was for the restaurant. This was a huge improvement over 12.2% margins in the same period in 2020, and the highest the chain has seen since the third quarter of 2015.</p>\n<p>\"We believe our key growth strategies will allow us to have 6,000 restaurants in North America with AUVs over $3 million, and as our unit volumes and sales rise, margins and returns will do the same,\" CFO Jack Hartung told Insider.<u></u></p>\n<p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/chiptole-ceo-brian-niccol-talks-delivery-profits-and-digital-dominance-2021-3\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Chipotle CEO Brian Niccol answers 9 questions about the chain's future including the fight for delivery profits, menu innovation, and franchising</a></em></p>\n<p>Chipotle says store margins were so high in part because of higher prices. In June, the fast-casual chain<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/chipotle-hiking-prices-across-menu-to-offset-higher-wages-2021-6\"> raised prices by about 4%</a>, increasing the price of the average Chipotle meal by about 30 to 40 cents. It says lower beef prices also contributed to higher margins.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/chipotle-mexican-grill-to-raise-wages-to-an-average-of-15-an-hour-2021-5\">Chipotle also raised wages this quarter,</a> boosting the average hourly pay to $15, an increase of $2 over the previous average of $13. When it raised prices, Chipotle said it was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/chipotle-is-raising-prices-but-its-not-slashing-ceo-compensation-2021-6\">prompted by rising labor costs.</a> The chain had previously <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/chipotle-will-raise-burrito-prices-if-a-15-minimum-wage-passes-2021-4\">warned that labor costs would be passed onto customers.</a> </p>\n<p>In the most recent earnings note, Chipotle mentions \"wage inflation\" as one factor that partially offset gains in profit. Labor is not the only cost going up for Chipotle. The note also mentions the price of avocados increasing, which alongside corn and other staples could impact Chipotle's bottom line as <a href=\"https://africa.businessinsider.com/news/taco-night-is-going-to-get-more-expensive-for-americans-this-summer-as-corn-prices/cl00p9h\">tortillas and guacamole become more expensive.</a> Chipotle says it has no further plans to raise prices.</p>\n<p><em>Do you have a story to share about a retail or restaurant chain? Meisenzahl)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5cc1ca30daa9a93d390b06b5?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn8@2020_3/2021/07/25/10-54-16-041_aa8187753be27304.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn39@2020_3/2021/07/25/10-54-25-234_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=kZb3RjRtB9s:XzQf6LNIvoE:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn75@2020_3/2021/07/25/10-54-25-704_4b748f37c78f15fb.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=kZb3RjRtB9s:XzQf6LNIvoE:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn56@2020_2/2021/07/25/10-54-24-283_f7ec4c89ac3c3f47.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn95@2020_6/2021/07/25/10-54-23-641_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=kZb3RjRtB9s:XzQf6LNIvoE:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn96@2020_4/2021/07/25/10-54-23-303_7ed24b63591c270a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/kZb3RjRtB9s":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn51@2020_5/2021/07/25/10-54-22-095_06e93ffff0beb656.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1627210446765},{"createdTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","updatedTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","title":"It's been 12 years since Congress last raised the minimum wage. As a McDonald's worker who makes just $10 an hour, I'm getting sick of Congress delaying another much-needed raise.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/mcdonalds-worker-minimum-wage-15-congress-starvation-wages-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fabe290729770012b97c1c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Workers are on strike at a McDondald&#39;s location in Detroit, demanding a raise in pay.\" height=\"1896\" width=\"3792\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Workers on strike at a McDonald&#39;s location in Detroit, demanding a raise in pay.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jarmier Owens</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>It&#39;s been 12 years since the federal minimum wage was increased to $7.25 per hour.</li>\n<li>I&#39;m a McDonald&#39;s worker who makes just $10 per hour.</li>\n<li>Millions of people across the country can no longer afford to wait - Congress must raise the minimum wage and lift workers out of poverty.</li>\n<li>Jarmier Owens has worked at a McDonald&#39;s location in Detroit for four years.</li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>For millions of workers across the country, it&#39;s been 12 years without a raise in the minimum wage.</p><p>12 years is a long time. In the past 12 years, we&#39;ve had three different presidents, six  Olympics, and seven Fast &#38; Furious movies. But in all that time, the federal minimum wage has stayed the same. The last time it was increased was on July 24, 2009, to the amount of just $7.25 an hour.</p><p>That means that companies like the one I work for, McDonald&#39;s, can continue to pay us starvation wages, even while they made nearly $5 billion in profits last year in the middle of a global pandemic. McDonald&#39;s CEO, Chris Kempczinksi, made $10.8 million last year while cooks and cashiers like me risked our lives serving burgers and fries for a paycheck that&#39;s hardly enough to keep a roof over our heads.</p><p>That&#39;s why on July 20, I joined my co-workers around the country in a strike to demand $15 per hour from companies like McDonald&#39;s. We&#39;re also calling on Congress to finally increase the federal minimum wage to $15 per hour.</p><h2>A living wage </h2><p>I&#39;ve heard a lot about the so-called economic recovery, but like many fast food workers across the country, I&#39;m struggling, and the pandemic has made things twice as hard. We have to do twice as much work to keep ourselves, our families and our customers safe. I&#39;m afraid of getting sick, but at the same time I&#39;m worried about paying for car insurance, food and rent.</p><p>There are some in Congress who say that states should set their own minimum wages or that it should be up to big corporations to decide base pay. But even while 10 states and some big companies have increased their minimum wages to $15 per hour, here in Michigan, the minimum wage is stuck at $9.65, and I&#39;m still making $10.</p><p>Even worse, Michigan has racist laws on the books. These laws, like Michigan&#39;s <a href=\"http://www.legislature.mi.gov/(S(lskutbeklmcztmtbsntwcchy))/mileg.aspx?page=getobject&objectname=mcl-123-13851385\">Local Government Labor Regulatory Limitation Act</a>, block Black and brown workers from getting a raise by preventing local governments from raising the local minimum wage. This happens even in cities that are far more expensive to live in than other parts of the state. With these kinds of laws in place, it sometimes feels like it&#39;s impossible for us to win, stuck between elected officials passing the responsibility to do their jobs back and forth. </p><p>But I got involved with the Fight for $15 and a Union because I refuse to accept that anything is impossible. It&#39;s time for a change, and that change can&#39;t be just for some - it has to apply to every single worker across the country.</p><p>We&#39;ll never have a recovery that is equal and just if some workers doing the same job with the same hours thrive, while others barely survive. We cannot leave anybody behind. $15 per hour is the bare minimum we need to get by, period. </p><p>Anything less than that is not only a slap in the face, it&#39;s a strain on the economy. Workers at other restaurants like Burger King are<a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/business/2021/07/13/burger-king-workers-quit/\"> walking off the job</a> as a group, tired of being treated without respect. Meanwhile, millions of families like mine are forced to rely on public assistance programs, at the<a href=\"https://laborcenter.berkeley.edu/the-public-cost-of-a-low-federal-minimum-wage/\"> cost</a> of nearly $107 billion taxpayer dollars a year. Raising the wage would get people back to work and save taxpayers&#39; money too.  </p><p>As a member of the Fight for $15 and a Union, I&#39;m fighting for a future where every community can thrive, regardless of race, gender or ZIP code. I know we can get there if big corporations and our elected leaders listen to our demands for $15 and a voice on the job. </p><p>We&#39;ve been fighting for years, and now I&#39;m asking all workers and allies to join us in the call. We need $15, and we need it now.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a years","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/federal-minimum-wage-raised-12-years-ago-wont-increase-soon-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6021758067d1e300113c4d41?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Bernie Sanders minimum wage\" height=\"1332\" width=\"1777\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sen. Bernie Sanders (I-VT) speaks during an event to introduce the Raise The Wage Act in the Rayburn Room at the U.S. Capitol January 16, 2019 in Washington, DC.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo by Chip Somodevilla/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The federal minimum wage was last raised on July 24, 2009 - 12 years ago.</li>\n<li>As legislators squabble over infrastructure, the minimum wage is still nowhere to be found.</li>\n<li>Democrats do still want to raise it, but the party is split on how and when to do it - and how much.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The federal minimum wage was last raised on July 24, 2009. Back then, &#34;I Gotta Feeling&#34; by the Black Eyed Peas was <a href=\"https://www.billboard.com/charts/hot-100/2009-07-25\">topping the charts</a> and &#34;Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince&#34; sat <a href=\"https://www.boxofficemojo.com/month/july/2009/\">atop of the box office</a>. Facebook was just starting to <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2009/01/22/facebook-now-nearly-twice-the-size-of-myspace-worldwide/\">eclipse</a> MySpace. </p><p>Times have changed. But the federal minimum wage of $7.25 hasn&#39;t.</p><p>In the last 12 years, a real movement to up the minimum to at least $15 has grown. <a href=\"https://fightfor15.org/about-us/\">Fight for 15</a>, a movement led by fast-food workers, began in 2012 - and it hasn&#39;t stopped campaigning. Politicians like <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-bernie-sanders-hopes-make-15-minimum-wage-reality-stimulus-2021-1\">Sen. Bernie Sanders</a> signed on to the cause. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/most-americans-support-15-minimum-wage-split-on-how-soon-2021-2\">Polling shows</a> that most Americans want a $15 minimum wage, and voters across the political spectrum reflected that: In 2020, red state Florida <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/florida-presidential-election-2020-live-vote-counts-results-2020\">voted</a> for Donald Trump to get another term - and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/florida-minimum-wage-rise-vote-amendment-15-tipped-employees-workers-2020-11\">voted</a> a $15 minimum wage into law.</p><p>Yet, progress has stalled. Eight moderate Democrats voted against a $15 minimum in President Joe Biden&#39;s first stimulus package. </p><p>A minimum wage increase has largely fallen off the Democrats&#39; radar as they prepare to advance as much as $4 trillion in new economic spending. Progressives including Sanders and Sen. Elizabeth Warren want to revisit it, while other members of their party aren&#39;t sure how to do it.</p><p>&#34;I&#39;m just not hearing much talk about it right now,&#34; Sen. Elizabeth Warren of Massachusetts told Insider. &#34;Democrats should tackle the minimum wage again. Too many people are struggling at the bottom end of the wage scale. Right now, all of the attention is around infrastructure.&#34; </p><p>Sanders indicated he could make another push later in the year. &#34;My intention is to do everything I can to make that happen,&#34; he told Insider.</p><p>But the party is still split about what to do. On the moderate side, Sen. Tom Carper of Delaware, who voted against the $15 minimum wage, told Insider that tying the minimum wage to changes in the consumer price index and inflation would &#34;be a good approach going forward.&#34; He didn&#39;t specify a number.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fb326917cf960019edfc3e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tom Carper\" height=\"3080\" width=\"4106\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sen. Tom Carper (D-DE) speaks during a hearing of the Finance Committee on June 17, 2020 in Washington, DC.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo by Anna Moneymaker-Pool/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>Democrats are stuck on the minimum wage</h2><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/map-the-last-time-each-state-raised-its-minimum-wage-2021-2\">Many states</a> have taken matters into their own hands and raised their own minimums, but 16 are at the federal rate and five default to the federal minimum.</p><p>A recent <a href=\"https://www.epi.org/blog/the-minimum-wage-has-lost-21-of-its-value-since-congress-last-raised-the-wage/\">report</a> from the left-leaning Economic Policy Institute finds that the federal minimum wage is worth 21% less than it was in 2009. </p><p>Arindrajit Dube, a professor of economics at the University of Massachusetts, Amherst, who has extensively studied the minimum wage and its impact on the economy, told Insider that the stagnant federal minimum - and some states defaulting to that rate - &#34;means that&#39;s there&#39;s still swaths of the country where essentially we don&#39;t have a wage standard.&#34;</p><div class=\"insider-raw-embed\"><iframe title=\"Real federal minimum wage\" aria-label=\"Interactive line chart\" id=\"datawrapper-chart-V4x33\" src=\"https://datawrapper.dwcdn.net/V4x33/2/\" scrolling=\"no\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"width: 0; min-width: 100% ; border: none;\" height=\"450\"></iframe><script type=\"text/javascript\">!function(){&#34;use strict&#34;;window.addEventListener(&#34;message&#34;,(function(e){if(void 0!==e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;]){var t=document.querySelectorAll(&#34;iframe&#34;);for(var a in e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;])for(var r=0;r&#60;t.length;r++){if(t[r].contentWindow===e.source)t[r].style.height=e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;][a]+&#34;px&#34;}}}))}();</script></div><p> </p><p>Raising the minimum wage, though, remains <a href=\"https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2021/04/22/most-americans-support-a-15-federal-minimum-wage/\">politically popular</a>, with <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/most-americans-support-15-minimum-wage-split-on-how-soon-2021-2\">poll</a> after <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/80-percent-americans-think-minimum-wage-is-too-low-2021-3\">poll</a> showing Americans support a higher wage.</p><p>&#34;I haven&#39;t seen any dampening of interest in raising the minimum wage by voters at large in any way. I actually absolutely agree that getting employers to compete for workers is critical. I think we also know, so is having a wage standard, a floor,&#34; Dube said. </p><p>&#34;The appetite to raise it is very high,&#34; Sen. Tim Kaine of Virginia told Insider, but he said Democrats still disagree on things like how fast it should be raised and whether a tipped wage should be left alone.</p><p>Kaine suggested that rising wages in the service sector as well as state moves to increase pay could be dampening urgency. President Joe Biden has said that employers are starting to compete for workers by hiking pay.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fb32a717cf960019edfc4b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mitt Romney congress\" height=\"683\" width=\"910\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sen. Mitt Romney (R-UT) speaks to reporters on Capitol Hill.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/J. Scott Applewhite</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>What is realistic?</h2><p>While $15 is the number progressives and the president have lined up behind, centrist senators think that&#39;s too high. For instance, Sens. Mitt Romney and Kyrsten Sinema <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/romney-sinema-are-working-on-a-minimum-wage-bill-together-2021-4\">said in April</a> that they were working on a bipartisan proposal to raise the minimum wage. They didn&#39;t specify a number, but Sen. Joe Manchin told <a href=\"https://www.huffpost.com/entry/minimum-wage-congress_n_60771d6fe4b001befb6fc904\">HuffPost</a> that he thought it was $11 -  a figure that Manchin, a key moderate, has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/manchin-poses-threat-to-progressives-plan-to-raise-the-minimum-wage\">previously signaled support for</a>.</p><p>That bill hasn&#39;t materialized so far. </p><p>&#34;I think $12 is better than $7.25,&#34; Dube said. &#34;And so I think having some kind of a compromise, which for example, Joe Manchin and others can live with, is much, much better than just not doing anything.&#34;</p><p>Romney and another Republican, Sen. Tom Cotton, have laid out a separate plan to raise it to $10 an hour over two years, tied to immigration enforcement. At the time, Republican Sen. Rob Portman told Insider he supported this plan.</p><p>Some Democrats appear to be revamping older ideas to attract GOP support. Sen. Ron Wyden, chair of the Senate Finance Committee, told Insider in a statement he still supports a backdoor approach that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stimulus-democrats-abandon-backup-15-hour-minimum-wage-hike-2021-2\">Democrats scrapped</a> in March. </p><p>It included tax credits for small businesses and tax penalties on large firms to incentivize them to raise wages, but experts at the time said it would be very difficult to implement and easily avoidable.</p><p>&#34;I&#39;ve continued to work on the carrot from my carrot-and-stick approach,&#34; Wyden said. &#39;I want to incentivize the smallest of small businesses - those with middle-class owners - to raise their workers&#39; wages.&#34;</p><p>He went on: &#34;[I] believe including this kind of carrot is key to getting Republicans on board because that&#39;s what we&#39;ve done in the past, and getting 60 votes,&#34; he said.</p><p>The amount of things Congress must address is piling up for September, making a federal minimum wage increase very unlikely before then. Lawmakers must pass new spending bills by September 30 or else the federal government shuts down. They also need to either suspend or raise the debt ceiling and deal with the end of stimulus programs like federal unemployment aid.</p><p>&#34;Going into the fall and end of the year before the holidays is kind of wide-open,&#34; Zach Moller, director of the economic program at the centrist think-tank Third Way, told Insider. &#34;Before then, we have a lot of things that must be done.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/federal-minimum-wage-raised-12-years-ago-wont-increase-soon-2021-7'>Business 18:54:06","updatedTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","title":"From clip art to Comic Sans: These screenshots from 25 years ago show just how much the internet has changed","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/web-from-1996-internet-25-years-ago-screenshots-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60f25f7571757b0018c6a38a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"clip art of a film reel and giant question mark\" height=\"577\" width=\"769\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Web Design Museum</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A report from Morgan Stanley analysts in 1996 predicted the prevalence of the internet. </li>\n<li>It said a person of intermediate web literacy was anyone who simply knew their own email address.</li>\n<li>From clip art to Comic Sans, screenshots show how different the internet looks 25 years later.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Morgan Stanley tech analysts Mary Meeker and Chris DePuy knew the world was on the cusp of something big in 1996. They drafted a 323-page report expressing their high hopes for the internet, saying it could be &#34;one of the hottest new markets to develop in years.&#34;</p><p>Looking back on the report now shows just how far the internet has come in 25 years.  </p><p>For starters, the report shows how rare some now-common internet activities were in the past. Among 150 million estimated PC users around the globe, the authors estimated 23% had used email for work, 6% had used the web, and 5% had used an online service. </p><p>&#34;We feel that e-mail, online/Web access may be ubiquitous for PC users within a decade,&#34; the authors wrote. &#34;At a minimum, e-mail should become pervasive. So should Internet/Web access: E-mail is the &#39;killer application&#39; of the Internet today, and browsing through information services the &#39;killer app&#39; of tomorrow.&#34;</p><p>Another marker of the web&#39;s progress came from the authors&#39; guide to the report for audiences of varying levels of internet literacy. </p><p>Meeker and DePuy defined a novice reader of the report as someone who had &#34;never heard of Motley Fool, CNET, or Yahoo.&#34; An intermediate audience was just anyone who &#34;knows [their] own email address.&#34;  </p><p>Take a glimpse at the internet of yesteryear with these screenshots of websites from 25 years ago.</p><p> </p><p> </p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tMcDonald's\n\t<figure>\n\t<img href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\"><strong>Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Social, or community, tokens are going to be the next big development in the crypto market and have the power to disrupt all kinds of traditional industries, according to RealVision CEO Raoul Pal. </p><p>Pal, who used to run hedge fund sales at Goldman Sachs, before retiring at 36 and devoting himself to other investments, told Insider in an interview he&#39;s so sure social tokens will boom that his company is planning to launch one over the next year. </p><p>Community tokens are a form of cryptocurrency that are linked to a company, an organization or even a person. The idea is the holders of that token will get perks from the issuer, such as exclusive content, access to group chats, or digital merchandise. </p><p>&#34;It&#39;s the biggest thing I&#39;ve ever seen, we all know how big crypto is, but within crypto, community tokens are going to change all business models,&#34; Pal said. </p><p>&#34;When you realise that tokenizing things changes the equation - it will not be long before Disney tokenize, because they have super fans, who want access to parts of the community. So you could have a Star Wars community, or a Disney animation community and people are fanatical about this,&#34; he said. </p><p>A sense of community has been a big factor in the growing adoption and popularity of bitcoin, the largest cryptocurrency by market value. </p><p>Pal said he believes the market in social tokens will go from being a &#34;billion dollar&#34; business  to a &#34;trillion dollar&#34; one in the next five to 10 years, so much so that he&#39;s planning one of his own. </p><p>&#34;I&#39;m trying to work on it. We have a great, amazing community of super smart people all around the world. They write to us all the time saying please can you create a token, we want to be a part of this, we want to be part of this kind of expert network of people that love finance and, you know, love investing and learning,&#34; Pal said. </p><p>Like many other digital assets, social tokens are decentralized and run on a blockchain network, much like traditional cryptocurrencies, or digital collectible items like non-fungible tokens. </p><p>One example is the <a href=\"https://www.rally.io/creator/KSK/\">Keisuke Honda&#39;s KSK Honda Coin</a> launched by <a href=\"https://www.rally.io/creator/KSK/\">Keisuke Honda</a>, a professional Japanese footballer and manager. This token gives fans access to exclusive video updates and private chats.</p><p>Another notable example is the $RAC token by musician and producer RAC. The community token enables his fans access to private discussions, merchandise and other exclusive content. </p><p>&#34;$RAC is a token built on ethereum that I want to give to fans who support the RAC project, and who want to build it alongside me. By rewarding my most loyal fans, we can create a community where tokens unlock access to various perks and exclusive content,&#34;  RAC said in a <a href=\"https://blog.ourzora.com/introducing-rac\">blog in 2020.</a> </p><p>Anyone can create a community token. Pal outlined the steps that a person, or company, would need to take to create an effective one. </p><p>&#34;You need to give [holders] benefits of community, utility of community so that they get discounted tickets, ability to get extra merchandise, ability to get access to NFTs, ability to have meet and greets, ability to chat with the artists, you need to generate all that ecosystem where everybody can connect and bond and everybody feels close to the center of the community, the influencer,&#34; he said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a that crypto is a lynchpin of the retail investment app&#39;s future, and a wallet could be in the works.</p><p>&#34;We&#39;ve been doing a lot of work behind the scenes to provide our crypto customers with the functionality that they&#39;ve been asking for,&#34; he said. &#34;We know you want wallets.&#34; </p><p>Users can expect a beta release of new crypto features at &#34;some point,&#34; he said, but did not provide any further timeline. It&#39;s a more tentative proclamation than he&#39;s previously made. Back in March, Tenev promised users a crypto wallet <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LlVa6SAFJzI\">&#34;as fast as possible.&#34;</a></p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/personal-finance/crypto-apps-to-use-instead-of-robinhood-2021-5\">Robinhood users currently can&#39;t transfer crypto</a> assets in and out of their account, potentially driving some customers to platforms like Coinbase. However, Tenev said that will be fixed as well.  </p><p>&#34;We want to introduce new features safely,&#34; he said. &#34;And there&#39;s a lot of items we have to get right from the start.&#34; </p><p>Tenev&#39;s statements came during Robinhood&#39;s public roadshow Saturday, where the company&#39;s top executives fielded questions from the public about its upcoming IPO, planned for Thursday.</p><p>It&#39;s been clear for awhile that Robinhood, founded in 2013, was veering into the crypto world. In the company&#39;s S-1, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/robinhood-ipo-dogecoin-crypto-revenue-trading-filing-price-risk-meme-2021-7\">it revealed that 17% of its first quarter revenue</a> came from cryptocurrency transactions. </p><p>But the company has admitted that crypto trading might be a liability. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/robinhood-ipo-dogecoin-crypto-revenue-trading-filing-price-risk-meme-2021-7\">Dogecoin made up 34%</a> of Robinhood&#39;s first quarter crypto-trading revenue, according to its IPO filing. If interest in the meme coin declines, the company said it could be a risk to the business. </p><p>Especially in light of the <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/s?q=robinhood\">many, many headlines</a> about the company, Robinhood&#39;s IPO is highly anticipated. In its regulatory <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/0001783879/000162828021013986/robinhoods-1a1.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">filing</a>, the company said it&#39;s aiming to raise as much as <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/robinhood-ipo-pricing-upcoming-stock-market-debut-offering-price-2021-7?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$2.3 billion</a>, with a market valuation at <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/robinhood-ipo-pricing-upcoming-stock-market-debut-offering-price-2021-7?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$35 billion</a> at the top range. Terry McAuliffe, who is seeking to reclaim his old job later this year.</p><p>Biden, who traveled a short distance from the White House to Arlington, Va., spoke before roughly 3,000 people for McAuliffe, a prodigious fundraiser and former Democratic National Committee chairman who served as governor of Virginia from 2014 to 2018.</p><p>In November, McAuliffe will face Republican Glenn Youngkin, a former private-equity chief, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/06/10/us/politics/virginia-governor.html\">in what is expected to be a competitive race</a> in a state that the president <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/virginia-presidential-election-2020-live-vote-counts-results-2020\">won easily</a> last year.</p><p>&#34;You&#39;re not gonna find anyone, I mean anyone, who knows how to get more done for Virginia than Terry,&#34; Biden said to the crowd. &#34;Off-year election, the country&#39;s looking. This is a big deal.&#34;</p><p><a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/joe-biden-health-government-and-politics-coronavirus-pandemic-4203984ca9812b0ea871a9719930d6a3\">According to The Associated Press</a>, protestors against an oil pipeline began to interrupt Biden, with the president <a href=\"https://twitter.com/AndrewSolender/status/1418726936470294532\">taking a dig</a> at his 2020 opponent, former President Donald Trump.</p><p>When the crowd started to boo and try to drown out the protestors with chants of &#34;Let&#39;s go, Joe,&#34; Biden responded, &#34;It&#39;s not a Trump rally ... let them holler. Kristi Noem&#39;s inner circle is packed with family, Trump aides, and connected South Dakotans. Meet the gatekeepers for her potential 2024 presidential run.</a></em></p><p>It will be crucial for Democrats to hold the Virginia Governor&#39;s Mansion as the party heads into the 2022 midterm election cycle. (New Jersey will also host a gubernatorial contest this year, with Democratic Gov. Phil Murphy favored to win that race, and California will hold a gubernatorial recall election on Sept. 14.)</p><p>For Republicans, the Virginia race provides an opportunity to potentially regain a foothold in a state that was once reliably conservative but has shifted to the left in recent cycles due to population growth and the increasing strength of the suburban vote.</p><p>The GOP has not won a statewide race in Virginia since 2009.</p><p>In Virginia, governors are barred from seeking a second consecutive term, so incumbent Democratic Gov. Ralph Northam cannot run for reelection.</p><p>Biden, in seeking to prop up McAuliffe and downballot Democrats, highlighted his stewardship of the country&#39;s continued recovery from the COVID-19 pandemic, which <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/these-5-key-numbers-are-currently-defining-the-biden-presidency-2021-7\">continues to earn him high marks</a> relative to his overall approval rating.</p><p>The president also <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stimulus-biden-signs-trillion-covid-relief-package-checks-direct-payments-2021-3\">touted</a> the $1.9 trillion COVID-19 relief package that issued a new set of stimulus checks and renewed enhanced unemployment insurance, among other measures.</p><p>But he then returned to his role as a party warrior, promoting McAuliffe and linking Youngkin to Trump.</p><p>&#34;You got to elect him again, and I mean this, not just for Virginia, for the country,&#34; Biden said. &#34;The country is looking, these off-year elections, the country&#39;s looking. This is a big deal. Terry and I share a lot in common. I ran against Donald Trump and so is Terry. And I whipped Donald Trump in Virginia and so will Terry.&#34;</p><p>He added: &#34;The guy Terry is running against is an acolyte of Donald Trump - for real, I mean it&#39;s just like, I don&#39;t know where these guys come from.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a newsletter.</a></li>\n</ul><p>The Biden administration is canceling two border wall contracts in the Laredo sector of the US-Mexico border that span roughly 31 miles, the Department of Homeland Security (DHS) <a href=\"https://www.dhs.gov/news/2021/07/23/dhs-cancel-laredo-sector-border-barrier-contracts\">said</a> on Friday.</p><p>Shortly after taking office in January, President Joe Biden paused border wall construction projects that were initiated by former President Donald Trump, <a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefing-room/presidential-actions/2021/01/20/proclamation-termination-of-emergency-with-respect-to-southern-border-of-united-states-and-redirection-of-funds-diverted-to-border-wall-construction/\">calling for</a> &#34;a review of all resources appropriated or redirected to construct&#34; the barrier.</p><p>Friday&#39;s announcement comes after the Biden administration last month <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/white-house-trump-returns-2-billion-military-border-wall-mexico-2021-6\">returned</a> to the military more than $2 billion in funding that the Trump administration had diverted for border wall construction.</p><p>The Biden administration&#39;s handling of Trump&#39;s border wall projects has unfolded at a slower pace due to funds having been allocated through different government agencies.</p><p>The contracts for the Laredo projects planned for 31 miles of border wall to be built along the Rio Grande, funded with DHS Fiscal Year 2020 appropriations.</p><p>However, construction on the projects had not yet started, nor had land acquisition been executed.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/georgia-election-donald-trump-fulton-county-investigation-fani-willis-2021-7\">Trouble is brewing for a Georgia county&#39;s criminal investigation into Donald Trump</a></em></p><section></section><p>&#34;DHS continues to review all other paused border barrier projects and is in the process of determining which projects may be necessary to address life, safety, environmental, or other remediation requirements and where to conduct environmental planning,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.dhs.gov/news/2021/07/23/dhs-cancel-laredo-sector-border-barrier-contracts\">the DHS release said</a>. &#34;The Administration also continues to call on Congress to cancel remaining border wall funding and instead fund smarter border security measures, like border technology and modernization of land ports of entry, that are proven to be more effective at improving safety and security at the border.&#34;</p><p>The Trump administration constructed roughly 450 miles of wall over four years, <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/government-and-politics-donald-trump-joe-biden-business-f12ef1a641bc326761656d4001054361\">according to The Associated Press</a>. However, only 52 miles of wall were built in areas where no barrier had previously existed.</p><p>The border between the US and Mexico stretches across more than 1,900 miles; some sections already had barriers prior to Trump taking office in 2017.</p><p>DHS is utilizing previously-appropriated funds to assess environmental issues that derived from previous wall construction, as well as reviewing land seizure cases to determine if those acquisitions are still necessary.</p><p>Biden&#39;s 2022 budget proposal <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/politics/biden-billion-border-infrastructure-migrant-care\">allocates</a> $1.2 billion for border infrastructure, including security technology, but <a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/omb/briefing-room/2021/06/11/fact-sheet-department-of-defense-and-department-of-homeland-security-plans-for-border-wall-funds/\">does not set aside funding</a> for additional wall construction.</p><p>GOP Gov. Greg Abbott of Texas last month <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/white-house-trump-returns-2-billion-military-border-wall-mexico-2021-6\">pledged to continue</a> building a wall at the border, though <a href=\"https://www.texastribune.org/2021/06/11/texas-border-wall/\">the legality of the move is being called into question</a>.</p><p data-el=\"text\">&#34;Only Congress and the president can fix our broken border,&#34; Abbott said at the time. &#34;But in the meantime, Texas is going to do everything possible, including beginning to make arrests, to keep our community safe.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Retail and fast-food workers say they&#39;re being harassed and assaulted. And small business owners report experiencing frustrated customers whose patience has evaporated. </p><p>All of this behavior is the result of a year and a half of fear and anxiety, according to <a href=\"https://drluana.com/\">Luana Marques</a>, an associate professor of psychiatry at Harvard Medical School. </p><p>&#34;We&#39;ve been skating thin ice in the past year, and if the weight [becomes] too much, the ice cracks. I think that&#39;s what we&#39;re seeing,&#34; she said. </p><h2>&#39;Everybody&#39;s just always mad&#39;</h2><p>In 2020, retail workers were called &#34;heroes&#34; and &#34;essential&#34; as they worked to supply meals or groceries amid a harrowing pandemic.</p><p>At the same time, they were tasked with carrying out one of the most complex social aspects of the pandemic: enforcing mask mandates. A survey of 4,187 McDonald&#39;s workers from last summer conducted by the Service Employees International Union found that 44% of respondents had been <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/workers-face-verbal-and-physical-assaults-from-anti-mask-customers-2020-7\">physically or verbally assaulted over mask mandates</a>. </p><p>Workers say <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/retail-workers-leaving-quit-over-nightmare-customers-low-pay-2021-5\">the abuse hasn&#39;t let up</a>, even as mask mandates have lifted in many parts of the country. A Starbucks barista in Louisiana recently told Insider&#39;s Mary Meisenzahl that the &#34;handful [of customers] that you get each day who will berate or abuse you can take a drastic toll on your mental well being.&#34;</p><p>That harassment, combined with low pay, is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/retail-workers-leaving-quit-over-nightmare-customers-low-pay-2021-5\">causing workers to leave their jobs</a>, leading to a labor crunch as society gradually reopens. </p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/a-theory-called-reallocation-friction-may-explain-the-labor-shortage-2021-5\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">An economic theory called &#39;reallocation friction&#39; may explain why employers are having a hard time finding workers - and why a full recovery could be years away</a></em></p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60faf2c2fc2536001820245d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Man wearing a face covering walking through a train station.\" height=\"3543\" width=\"4724\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>&#34;Either they&#39;re upset they have to wear the mask or they&#39;re upset someone else isn&#39;t wearing the mask,&#34; one flight attendant told Insider.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Richard Baker/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The situation isn&#39;t much better on airplanes. After aggression over mask compliance spiked last summer, the Federal Aviation Administration began tracking unruly passenger reports, according to <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2021/05/28/1001385922/the-faa-has-seen-a-significantly-higher-number-of-unruly-passenger-reports-in-20\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"9dfce2d202c0b20da9f6fa0328dc2610\">NPR.</a> Since January 2021, the FAA has received <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/faa-charged-fines-up-to-15000-for-assaulting-flight-attendants-2021-5\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"a9dc4fbf60d5a81a875fb0eb7fbde8c8\">2,500 reports of unruly behavior,</a> leading to thousands of dollars in fines for passengers. </p><p>FAA spokesperson Ian Gregor told NPR that the number of reports is now &#34;significantly higher&#34; than in the past, which coincides with what flight attendants are seeing on planes: Insider&#39;s Allana Akhtar spoke with several flight attendants who described <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/flight-attendants-are-burned-out-as-passenger-violence-soars-2021-6\">witnessing &#34;unprecedented&#34; passenger violence</a> as travel returns and planes begin to fill back up. </p><p>&#34;It seems that everybody is angry at everybody 24/7,&#34; Colleen Burns, a representative with the Association of Flight Attendants union, told Insider. &#34;One little thing sets them over the edge, either they&#39;re upset they have to wear the mask or they&#39;re upset someone else isn&#39;t wearing the mask.&#34; </p><p>Some small businesses are also noticing a change in customer behavior. Paul Collurafici, the owner of <a href=\"https://www.tattoofactory.com/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"4e63630cd91d121cb4a8708f8967ee22\">Tattoo Factory</a>, a piercing and tattoo studio in Chicago&#39;s Uptown neighborhood, told Insider that many of his customers are frustrated and short-tempered when they learn of the restrictions his business has had to put in place due to the pandemic. </p><p>&#34;We have a large amount of people that don&#39;t want to wait, don&#39;t want to follow the rules,&#34; he said. &#34;Everybody&#39;s just always mad.&#34; </p><h2>Fight or flight</h2><p>Marques, the Harvard psychologist, said that the pandemic has understandably caused fear and anxiety in a lot of people, which leads to the activation of the amygdala, the fight-or-flight part of our brains. </p><p>&#34;Patience is the ability to restrain your emotions a little bit, right? And you need your thinking brain there. You need to be able to assess the situation, you need to be able to just slow down and not let your emotional brain take off,&#34; she said. &#34;But if you walk into a store ... and you&#39;re already on edge, you&#39;re more likely to get impatient because you&#39;re not able to press &#39;pause&#39; on your emotional brain.&#34; </p><p>Marques explained that even though life is gradually opening back up and the most frightening days of the pandemic are hopefully behind us, people are still &#34;riding really high cortisol,&#34; which means they&#39;re more on edge and quicker to reach what she called a &#34;boiling point.&#34; </p><p>She said one way to help people recalibrate their emotions and stop resorting to aggression is to shift their perspective. </p><p>&#34;When we&#39;re anxious, our lenses are distorted. We tend to magnify or &#39;catastrophize,&#39;&#34; she said. &#34;Widen your lenses and try to collect more data - that tends to also cool off the brain a little bit.&#34; </p><div Kay Ivey of Alabama, who for much of the coronavirus pandemic resisted public-health measures, criticized her state&#39;s unvaccinated population.</p><p>&#34;I don&#39;t know, you tell me,&#34; she said when asked what it would take to get more people vaccinated. &#34;Folks supposed to have common sense. Senate Minority leader <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mitch-mcconnell-gop-debt-ceiling-democrats-biden-congress-2021-7?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">Mitch McConnell</a> led this movement, urging people on Tuesday, to ignore the &#34;demonstrably bad advice&#34; which spreads mistrust of the vaccines, and said, &#34;If there is anybody out there willing to listen: Get vaccinated.&#34;</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cisa-kenrda-martin-covid-vaccine-bureaucracy-2021-6?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Meet the government worker who cut through months&#39; worth of federal bureaucracy in 10 days to help millions of Americans get vaccinated</a></em></p><p>Ron DeSantis - Governor of Florida, where <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/1-in-5-covid-19-cases-happening-in-florida-alone-2021-7?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">1 in 5 Covid cases</a> in the USA are -  told the public in the Trump heartland: &#34;If you are vaccinated, fully vaccinated, the chance of you getting seriously ill or dying from COVID is effectively zero ... These vaccines are saving lives,&#34; he said during a press conference.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ded1cc4a93e2001912996c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"donald trump ron desantis\" height=\"1500\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Donald Trump and Florida Governor Ron DeSantis on November 26, 2019 in Sunrise, Florida.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Joe Raedle/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Alabama Senator Tommy Tuberville is another high-profile Republican exhibiting a change in tune. He took to Twitter July 21 to say that the vaccines are &#34;effective, safe, and don&#39;t cost you a dime.&#34;</p><p>Joining the Republican U-turn, House Minority Whip Steve Scalise (R-La.)  - who had <a href=\"https://www.speaker.gov/newsroom/22221-1\">previously attempted to block Senate funding for the COVID-19</a> vaccine in tandem with his anti-vaxx stance - received his dose of the vaccine, telling people they should get theirs and that it is &#34;safe and effective.&#34; </p><p>He added: &#34;When you talk to people who run hospitals, in New Orleans or other states, 90% of people in hospitals with Delta variant have not been vaccinated. That&#39;s another signal the vaccine works,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.nola.com/news/coronavirus/article_f569bf58-e970-11eb-8456-7ba1aef698cd.html\">The Times-Picayune reported</a>. </p><p>President Biden and the head of the CDC, have called the current state of COVID-19 in the USA the &#34;pandemic of the unvaccinated.&#34; </p><p>Three strongly GOP states account for 40% of Covid cases - Florida, Missouri, and Texas - announced White House pandemic response coordinator Jeff Zients at a press briefing on July 21. </p><p>Rob Wilson, former GOP strategist and founder of the Lincoln Project, said on Twitter that he believes this change in tone is a polling strategy - the result of a realization that it may not be politically palpable to reject the vaccine whilst COVID-19 deaths and cases surge.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Rick Wilson  (@TheRickWilson) <a most recent poll, 45% of respondents disapproved of Biden&#39;s job performance, while 5% did not express an opinion.</p><p>Biden&#39;s approval decline comes as the nation seems to have hit a wall in increasing vaccination rates, along with <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/majority-americans-concerned-about-delta-variant-covid-poll-2021-7\">the growing unease</a> about the spread of the COVID-19 Senate has made enormous progress on a roughly $1 trillion bipartisan infrastructure bill, but the legislation has not cleared the chamber yet, and Democrats also <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/these-5-key-numbers-are-currently-defining-the-biden-presidency-2021-7\">hope to push through</a> a separate party-line $3.5 trillion infrastructure bill through the budget reconciliation process.</p><p>While Biden still enjoys overwhelming support among Democrats, at 90% approval, his approval rating among Independents dropped to 48% in the latest poll, the first time it has dropped below 50% with the latter group since taking office in January.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a quarter average approval rating was 53.3%, which is higher than both former President Bill Clinton (44%) and former President Donald Trump (38.8%), per Gallup data.</p><p>However, the president&#39;s second quarter average was below that of former President Barack Obama (62%) and former President George W. Bush (55.8%).</p><p>From the 1950s to the 1980s, presidents often boasted higher approval ratings than what currently exists today, the result of less stringent political polarization - former Presidents Dwight D. Kennedy both averaged approval ratings exceeding 70% during their second quarters, <a href=\"https://news.gallup.com/poll/352733/biden-approval-drops-lowest-date.aspx\">according to uptick in crime in certain Boston neighborhoods appears to be linked to the introduction of Airbnb rentals, according to a <a href=\"https://journals.plos.org/plosone/article?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0253315\">study out of Northeastern University</a>.</li>\n<li>Researchers said the uptick in violence was related to the lack stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>An uptick in violence in certain neighborhoods in Boston appears to be linked to an increase of Airbnb rentals in the areas over the span of several years, according to a study published this month.</p><p>The study was published July 14 by researchers at Northeastern University in Boston, <a href=\"https://www.boston.com/news/local-news/2021/07/23/increases-in-airbnb-listings-linked-to-more-violent-crime-in-boston-neighborhoods-study-suggests/\">Boston.com reported on Friday.</a></p><p>Because the increase in violent crime occurred several years after Airbnb rentals were introduced to the area, the researchers linked the uptick in crime to a disruption in the social dynamic in the communities created by the increase in short-term rentals, and not to an increase in tourism.</p><p>&#34;Airbnb prevalence in a neighborhood appears to be associated with increases in violence, but not with public social disorder or private conflict,&#34; the study found.</p><p>Representatives for Airbnb did not immediately return Insider&#39;s request for comment Saturday.</p><p>There were more than 6,000 Airbnb rentals in Boston in 2018, according to the research, more than double the number the city had in 2014, the study said. </p><p>&#34;What&#39;s interesting about social organization is that it&#39;s not really about going over to each other&#39;s houses for backyard barbecues, it&#39;s not knowing all your neighbors&#34; Daniel O&#39;Brien, one of the researchers who conducted the study, told Boston.com. &#34;It&#39;s as little as being familiar strangers.&#34;</p><p>Airbnb <a href=\"https://news.airbnb.com/airbnb-and-the-neighborhoods-our-hosts-and-guests-call-home/\">in a blog post last week</a> appeared to defend itself against claims presented by the researchers.</p><p>&#34;The study examines a handful of districts in Boston only, and then extrapolates that into nationwide generalizations without providing detailed evidence,&#34; the company said.</p><p>Airbnb also claimed researchers used &#34;inaccurate data&#34; and a &#34;flawed methodology&#34; to reach their conclusions, arguing that researchers didn&#39;t control other variables, like new construction in neighborhoods and the &#34;overall economic conditions.&#34; </p><p>&#34;Over the last year-plus, various reports indicate the unfortunate trend that crime has risen in many American cities (even as travel and tourism, including short-term rentals, have suffered in urban markets). There are many complex issues that contribute to rises and falls in crime rates that require serious research to help inform and guide public policy work,&#34; the company said in the blog post.</p><p>It added: &#34;As a society, we should be working to advance serious research. rules","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-19-cases-us-surge-highest-since-may-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fc138617cf960019ee01ac?format=jpeg\"
