18:54:06","updatedTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","title":"Biden has been assessing the legality of canceling $50,000 in student debt for millions of Americans. After several months, there's still no word.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/student-debt-cancellation-education-justice-department-reviews-biden-status-unknown-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fada5efc253600182012f8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Joe Biden\" height=\"3142\" width=\"4190\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Joe Biden.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Evan Vucci</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Early in his term, Biden asked the Education and Justice Depts. to review the legality of canceling student debt.</li>\n<li>They are assessing $50,000 in student debt being canceled per person, and no update has been released.</li>\n<li>Some Democrats remain adamant that Biden can cancel student debt under the Higher Education Act.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Imagine getting your student debt canceled. President Joe Biden campaigned on it, vowing that he would &#34;immediately&#34; wipe out thousands of dollars in debt for every borrower if he was elected.</p><p>Six months in, though, the White House is still reviewing the legality of doing that.</p><p>Early in his term, Biden <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/student-loan-debt-cancellation-payment-pause-borrowers-disabilities-defrauded-2021-6#asked-the-justice-and-education-departments-to-review-his-authority-to-cancel-student-debt-2\">asked</a> the Education and Justice Departments to review his legal authority to cancel $50,000 in student debt per borrower by executive order. The $50,000 figure wasn&#39;t his idea; Sen. Elizabeth Warren campaigned on canceling that amount, while Biden said he&#39;d wipe out a more moderate $10,000 per borrower. </p><p>During a CNN town hall in February, Biden began to change his tune, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-wont-cancel-student-debt-heres-why-go-big-economy-2021-2\">saying</a> he didn&#39;t believe he had the legal ability to cancel $50,000 per borrower.</p><p>Soon afterward, White House Press Secretary Jen Psaki <a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefing-room/press-briefings/2021/02/17/press-briefing-by-press-secretary-jen-psaki-and-deputy-national-security-advisor-for-cyber-and-emerging-technology-anne-neuberger-february-17-2021/\">said</a> in February that Biden had asked the Justice Department to conduct a review on his ability to cancel $50,000 in student debt per borrower using executive powers. </p><p>White House Chief of Staff Ron Klain told Politico in April that Biden had also asked Education Secretary Miguel Cardona to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-wants-to-cancel-student-loan-debt-ron-klain-says-2021-4\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"05c21c044de677fdb8e598f30016a856\">create a memo</a> on the president&#39;s legal authority to forgive $50,000 in student loans per person. He said Biden will &#34;look at that legal authority.&#34;</p><p>&#34;He&#39;ll look at the policy issues around that, and he&#39;ll make a decision,&#34; Klain said. &#34;He hasn&#39;t made a decision on that either way, and, in fact, he hasn&#39;t yet gotten the memos that he needs to start to focus on that decision.&#34;</p><p>So when will Biden be getting those memos?</p><p>Neither the Education nor the Justice Department responded to Insider&#39;s requests for comment, leaving borrowers with no timeline on when Biden will get the information he needs to make a decision on broad student-debt cancellation. The White House also did not respond to a request for comment.</p><p>In terms of what experts think will come of the reviews, opinions differ. Mark Kantrowitz, an expert on student loans who has published bestselling books on the subject, told Insider <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/student-loan-debt-cancellation-biden-jobs-economic-recovery-education-2021-7\">last month</a> that if the departments are truly conducting these reviews, they will find Biden &#34;does not have that authority&#34; under the Higher Education Act.</p><p>&#34;He has asked the Department of Justice and US Department of Education to give them a report on whether he has that authority,&#34; Kantrowitz said, &#34;and if they&#39;re honest, they&#39;re going to say &#39;no.&#39;&#34;</p><p>Kantrowitz said the Democrats pushing for $50,000 in student debt cancellation are taking a section of the Higher Education Act out of context, and it&#39;s Congress that has &#34;the power of the purse&#34; and ultimately holds the authority to wipe out debt. He referred to the <a href=\"https://www.govinfo.gov/content/pkg/USCODE-2011-title20/pdf/USCODE-2011-title20-chap28-subchapIV-partB-sec1082.pdf\">section</a> of the Act that says the Education Secretary can &#34;...modify, compromise, waive, or release any right, title, claim, lien, or demand, however acquired, including any equity or any right of redemption.&#34;</p><p>Seth Frotman, executive director of the Student Borrower Protection Center, which protects borrowers&#39; rights, told Insider <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/student-loan-debt-forgiveness-biden-campaign-promises-education-department-2021-6\">last month</a> that the findings should be &#34;crystal clear.&#34;</p><p>&#34;Any kind of deliberate, straightforward reading of the Higher Education Act makes it very clear that the Education Secretary has broad discretion to cancel debt and help student loan borrowers,&#34; Frotman said.</p><p>The leading Democrats pushing for $50,000 in student debt cancellation - Sen. Warren and Senate Majority Leader Chuck Schumer - agree with Frotman. Since Biden took office, they have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/warren-schumer-biden-cancel-student-debt-executive-order-keep-pressure-2021-3\">remained adamant</a> that the Higher Education Act would permit the president to wipe out student debt for borrowers, and they are urging him to act as soon as possible, even before the results of the reviews are released.</p><p>Warren previously told Insider that she thinks the reviews are a step in the right direction, and for this article, referred Insider to a <a href=\"https://www.warren.senate.gov/imo/media/doc/Ltr%20to%20Warren%20re%20admin%20debt%20cancellation.pdf\">letter</a> from the Legal Services Center of Harvard Law School that detailed the Education Secretary&#39;s legal ability to cancel student debt. </p><p>&#34;President Biden can cancel $50,000 of student loan debt with the stroke of a pen,&#34; Warren told Insider in June. &#34;He doesn&#39;t need Congress to act, he can do it on his own, and I hope that&#39;s what he&#39;s going to do.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/student-debt-cancellation-education-justice-department-reviews-biden-status-unknown-2021-7'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/60fada5efc253600182012f8?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"095b97f96626dd5d923777f5bbb5697a","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn18@2020_2/2021/07/25/10-54-19-417_f59f20e1687c09f7.webp","destWidth":4190,"destHeight":3142,"sourceBytes":199072,"destBytes":199072,"author":"asheffey@businessinsider.com (Ayelet Sheffey)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/60fada5efc253600182012f8?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn18@2020_2/2021/07/25/10-54-19-417_f59f20e1687c09f7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn39@2020_3/2021/07/25/10-54-25-234_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=R2psazNsttY:2bhywxa3MgI:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn16@2020_5/2021/07/25/10-54-24-793_4206b9da85b380f8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=R2psazNsttY:2bhywxa3MgI:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn39@2020_4/2021/07/25/10-54-26-205_c425b8b8bc171234.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn95@2020_6/2021/07/25/10-54-23-641_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=R2psazNsttY:2bhywxa3MgI:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn63@2020_6/2021/07/25/10-54-23-609_8ad08f7be733e515.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/R2psazNsttY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn80@2020_1/2021/07/25/10-54-22-103_d2b1a893e287e843.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1627210446772},{"createdTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","updatedTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","title":"A 19-year-old restaurant boss started out buttering toast for $9.25 an hour - now, he earns $50,000 and manages 22 people. Here's what his workday looks like.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/labor-shortage-job-diary-teenage-restaurant-boss-earns-50k-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60f843da2a723b0011e5076a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Jason Cabrera smiles while wearing a baseball cap and a black t-shirt while working at his restaurant.\" height=\"2001\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Jason Cabrera, 19, is the general manager for a Layne&#39;s Chicken Fingers restaurant in Allen, Texas.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zerb Mellish for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Jason Cabrera, 19, earns $50,000 a year and manages 22 people at Layne&#39;s Chicken Fingers in Texas. </li>\n<li>Laynes&#39; CEO said he has made three teenagers managers this year amid the labor shortage. </li>\n<li>Cabrera said some customers are &#34;shocked&#34; at his young age. Here&#39;s what his day looks like.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Jason Cabrera became a manager of a Texas fast-food restaurant just one week after his 19th birthday. He started out buttering toast and washing dishes for $9.25 per hour, and now earns $50,000 a year in his senior role. </p><p>Cabrera, who joined the Allen branch of <a href=\"https://www.layneschickenfingers.com/\">Layne&#39;s Chicken Fingers</a> in late 2018, took the job in January, as a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fast-food-retail-labor-shortage-teenagers-managers-wage-laynes-texas-2021-6\">severe labor shortage</a> pushed the restaurant&#39;s CEO to promote three of its teenage employees to managers.</p><p>The young manager took Insider through his average workday, from making a lemonade batch at 8 a.m. to checking in with some of the 22 employees he manages.</p><p><strong>At 8 a.m., Cabrera gets into the restaurant before his team arrives and makes a big batch of lemonade for customers. </strong></p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60f8452d0729770012b91340?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A parking lot outside a fast food restaurant with a white and red facade on a sunny day.\" height=\"2001\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Layne&#39;s Chicken Fingers restaurant in Allen, Texas.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zerb Mellish for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>By 10.30 a.m., all team members have arrived - Cabrera usually manages about eight per shift - and the restaurant is open for its first customers. </p><p>Cabrera said that managing 22 people, all aged between 16 and 21 years, forced him to mature quickly. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60f848712a723b0011e50963?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A restaurant worker wears a black and white baseball cap while working\" height=\"2001\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Cabrera&#39;s staff are all aged between 16 and 21 years.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zerb Mellish for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>&#34;When I started working I was still a young kid that liked to have fun,&#34; he said. &#34;That was the problem. I had too much fun but I guess as I started getting into the role and whatnot, I matured so quickly without really noticing.&#34;</p><p><strong><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60f845b70729770012b9137d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Two men work in a restaurant kitchen deep frying food.\" height=\"2001\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Cabrera said that he is on his feet from about 8 a.m. to 3 p.m. every day.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zerb Mellish for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></p><p><strong>From 10.30 a.m. to 3 p.m., Cabrera is constantly moving, checking in with his team, and dealing with guests.</strong></p><p>Asked whether he finds being on his feet all day tiring, Cabrera said that he doesn&#39;t &#34;feel anything&#34; because he&#39;s &#34;really young.&#34;</p><p>&#34;Probably once I, you know, start getting older then I&#39;ll start having back problems,&#34; he said.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60f847002a723b0011e508d9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Two customers in a fast food restaurant with red brick walls are served their food.\" height=\"2001\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Cabrera said that Tuesdays are often very busy with customers when Layne&#39;s offers promotional deals.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zerb Mellish for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>On Tuesdays, when Layne&#39;s offers a range of meal deals, including discounts of up to 20%, the restaurant is usually busier.</strong></p><p>Cabrera said he particularly enjoys these days because he gets to interact with more guests. </p><p>&#34;It&#39;s something I get to look forward to every week,&#34; he said. &#34;I really love seeing our parking lot filled with a bunch of cars.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60f847620729770012b91442?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A fast food worker wears a grey top and black and white baseball cap while dispensing a soft drink.\" height=\"2001\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Cabrera manages up to eight workers in any given shift.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zerb Mellish for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Cabrera said he enjoys dealing with &#34;shocked&#34; customers who asked to see the manager and don&#39;t expect to see &#34;a 19-year-old kid running a whole store.&#34; Several customers have asked him for his age. </p><p>&#34;I love seeing the reaction. It&#39;s really funny,&#34; he said. &#34;They start complimenting me and just letting me know, hey man, when I was your age I wasn&#39;t doing any of that stuff.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60f8472b2a723b0011e508e9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A fast-food worker prepares fries for the deep-fat fryer in a restaurant kitchen.\" height=\"2001\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Cabrera helps out in the kitchen and usually prepares a big batch of lemonade for customers when he arrives at 8 a.m.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zerb Mellish for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>At 3 p.m., Cabrera retires to the restaurant&#39;s office to do paperwork, which includes calculating labor costs, ordering inventory, and tallying up sales and drive-through times</strong>.</p><p>&#34;I crunch those numbers down every week. So the next week we have our corporate meetings here at the office and we go over those numbers,&#34; he said. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60f848a20729770012b914ce?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A fast food restaurant interior with light wood panels and red walls.\" height=\"2001\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Allen branch of Layne&#39;s Chicken Fingers is one of eight across Texas.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zerb Mellish for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Cabrera said he has spent much of his time recently trying to recruit workers. Garrett Reed, Layne&#39;s CEO, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/labor-shortage-chicken-prices-laynes-chicken-fingers-texas-inflation-2021-7\">previously told Insider</a> that he <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/restaurant-prices-labor-shortage-worker-wages-food-2021-6\">hiked wages</a> for shift managers by 17% to $14-per-hour to entice applicants amid an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/labor-shortage-restaurants-hospitality-temporarily-close-food-work-jobs-employment-2021-7\">industry-wide labor shortage</a>. </p><p><strong><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60f847ee2a723b0011e50939?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A fast food worker wears a grey t-shirt and red baseball cap while in the restaurant kitchen.\" height=\"2001\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Cabrera said that much of his time recently has been spent trying to find workers.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zerb Mellish for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></p><p><strong>At 4 p.m., Cabrera hands over to a shift manager and often goes to watch a baseball game. </strong></p><p>After work, Cabrera watches the Texas Rangers in action. His new paycheck means he can do this far more regularly. </p><p>&#34;I would only to go to one game a season but now I go to like 12 games a season,&#34; he said. </p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/business-economy-worker-shortage-restaurants-rights-wages-protest-2021-7\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">I&#39;m a millionaire businessman who was arrested for protesting with restaurant workers. We demand better wages for the employees running our economy.</a></em></p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60f848210729770012b91499?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A fast food restaurant manager wears a black t-shirt and baseball cap while sitting at a high table.\" height=\"2000\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Cabrera said that he has matured quickly since taking on the general manager role.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zerb Mellish for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Cabrera said he is saving part of his $50,000 annual salary to buy his parents a house and eventually open his own Layne&#39;s franchise. </p><p>&#34;If I&#39;m smart with my money, which I have been,&#34; he said. &#34;I&#39;ll probably get there real quick.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57a0ef5d88e4a727008bc8aa?format=jpeg\" alt=\"caroline kennedy\" height=\"688\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Caroline Kennedy.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Marc Andrew Deley/Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>President Biden is set to nominate Caroline Kennedy as ambassador to Australia, <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2021/07/23/politics/biden-caroline-kennedy-australia/index.html\">per a CNN report</a>.</li>\n<li>Kennedy served as US ambassador to Japan under then-President Barack Obama from 2013 to 2017.</li>\n<li>She is a longtime friend of Biden, who served in the Senate with her uncle, the late Ted Kennedy.</li>\n<li><a href=\"http://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/10-things-in-politics?utm_source=bullets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">Sign up for the 10 Things in Politics daily newsletter.</a></li>\n</ul><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\">President Joe Biden is set to nominate Caroline Kennedy to become the next ambassador to Australia, <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2021/07/23/politics/biden-caroline-kennedy-australia/index.html\">according to a CNN report</a>.</p><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\">Kennedy, the daughter of former President John F. Kennedy and former first lady Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis, served as ambassador to Japan from 2013 to 2017 under then-President Barack Obama.</p><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\">She is a longtime friend and political ally of Biden, <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=n0M36lJccCM\">and spoke</a> during the Democratic National Convention last summer.</p><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\">A White House spokesperson declined to comment on the nomination, saying that additional ambassadors would be revealed once the vetting process was finished.</p><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\">Kennedy&#39;s appointment would highlight the Biden administration&#39;s continued emphasis on Asia-Pacific relations, especially as China continues to flex its muscle on the international stage.</p><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\">The US and Australia long have maintained a robust diplomatic relationship, accentuated by close trade ties between the two countries.</p><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\"><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-white-house-administration-maga-alumni-network-database-2021-7\">Where is Trump&#39;s White House staff now? We created a searchable database of more than 328 top staffers to show where they all landed</a></em></p><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\">During her stint in Tokyo, Kennedy worked on economic and trade affairs, among other issues.</p><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\">Before joining the Obama administration, Kennedy, an author and attorney, worked at the Metropolitan Museum of Art and served as director of the Office of Strategic Partnerships for the New York City Department of Education.</p><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\">She has also sat on the boards of numerous nonprofits, and <a href=\"https://www.jfklibrary.org/about-us/jfk-library-foundation/board-of-directors\">serves</a> as the honorary president of the John F. Kennedy Library Foundation.</p><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\">Biden&#39;s relationship with the Kennedy family runs deep.</p><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\">The president served in the Senate with Caroline&#39;s uncle, Ted Kennedy of Massachusetts, throughout his entire 36-year tenure in the upper chamber.</p><p data-paragraph-id=\"paragraph_2037412B-5B62-3B8E-C01D-D43C82BB734A\" data-act-id=\"paragraph_0\">Biden has also <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2021/07/21/politics/ambassadors-canada-slovenia-austria-biden/index.html\">nominated</a> Sen. Kennedy&#39;s widow, Victoria Kennedy, to become the next ambassador to Austria.</p><p>He has spoke of the pivotal roles that John F. Kennedy and Ted Kennedy played in his life, reflecting on their Irish Catholic upbringing and their legacy of public service.</p><p>During a dedication for Sen. Kennedy in 2015, Biden said that without the senator&#39;s support, he would have walked away from his political career after losing his wife and daughter in a 1972 car accident shortly after his election to the Senate. The accident also resulted in severe injuries to his two sons, Beau and Hunter.</p><p>&#34;It&#39;s close to certain I would have never been sworn in as a United States senator if not for your father, your father&#39;s encouragement,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aL7Kb4I63q0\">Biden told the Kennedy children</a> at the time. &#34;I didn&#39;t show up the day I was to be sworn in. It was your father, your father, who along with [Democratic Sen.] Mike Mansfield [of Montana], sent the secretary of the Senate to a hospital in Wilmington, Delaware, to swear me in with my boys.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-caroline-kennedy-ambassador-australia-report-2021-7'>Business 18:54:06","updatedTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","title":"A man used AI to bring back his deceased fiancé. But the creators of the tech warn it could be dangerous and used to spread misinformation.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/man-used-ai-to-talk-to-late-fiance-experts-warn-tech-could-be-misused-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fc509e17cf960019ee03f3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"GPT-3 is a computer program that attempts to write like humans.\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>GPT-3 is a computer program that attempts to write like humans.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Fabrizio Bensch/ Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A man used artificial intelligence (AI) to create a chatbot that mimicked his late fiancé. </li>\n<li>The groundbreaking AI technology was designed by Elon Musk&#39;s research group OpenAI. </li>\n<li>OpenAI has long warned that the technology could be used for mass information campaigns. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>After Joshua Barbeau&#39;s fiancé passed away, he spoke to her for months. Or, rather, he spoke to a chatbot programmed to sound exactly like her. </p><p><a href=\"https://www.sfchronicle.com/projects/2021/jessica-simulation-artificial-intelligence/\">In a story for the San Francisco Chronicle</a>, Barbeau detailed how Project December, a software that uses artificial intelligence technology to create hyper-realistic chatbots, recreated the experience of speaking with his late fiancé. All he had to do was plug in old messages and give some background information, and suddenly the model could emulate his partner with stunning accuracy.</p><p>It may sound like a miracle (<a href=\"https://www.imdb.com/title/tt2290780/\">or a Black Mirror episode)</a>, but the AI creators warn that the same technology could be used to fuel mass misinformation campaigns.</p><p>Project December is powered by GPT-3, an AI model designed by the Elon Musk-backed research group OpenAI. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/youtube-algorithm-continues-to-push-misinformation-study-finds-2021-7\">By consuming massive datasets of human-created text</a> (<a href=\"https://openai.com/blog/better-language-models/#sample8\">Reddit threads were particularly helpful)</a>, GPT-3 can imitate human writing, producing everything from academic papers to letters from former lovers.</p><p>It&#39;s some of the most sophisticated - and dangerous - language-based AI programming to date. </p><p>When OpenAI released GPT-2, the predecessor to GPT-3, <a href=\"https://openai.com/blog/better-language-models/#sample8\">the group wrote</a> that it can potentially be used in &#34;malicious ways.&#34; The organization anticipated bad actors using the technology could automate &#34;abusive or faked content on social media,&#34; &#34;generate misleading news articles,&#34; or &#34;impersonate others online.&#34;  </p><p>GPT-2 could be used to &#34;unlock new as-yet-unanticipated capabilities for these actors,&#34; the group wrote.  </p><p>OpenAI staggered the release of GPT-2, and still restricts access to the superior GPT-3, in order to &#34;give people time&#34; to learn the &#34;societal implications&#34; of such technology.  </p><p>Misinformation is already rampant on social media, even with GPT-3 not widely available. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/youtube-algorithm-continues-to-push-misinformation-study-finds-2021-7\">A new study found that YouTube&#39;s algorithm</a> still pushes misinformation, and the nonprofit Center for Countering Digital Hat<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/12-anti-vaxxers-responsible-for-most-disinformation-online-study-says-2021-7\">e recently identified 12 people responsible</a> for sharing 65 percent of COVID-19 conspiracy theories on social media. Dubbed the &#34;Disinformation Dozen,&#34; they have millions of followers.  </p><p>As AI continues to develop, Oren Etzioni, CEO of the non-profit, bioscience research group, Allen Institute, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/youtube-algorithm-continues-to-push-misinformation-study-finds-2021-7\">previously told Insider</a> it will only become harder to tell what&#39;s real. </p><p>&#34;The question &#39;Is this text or image or video or email authentic?&#39; is going to become increasingly difficult to answer just based on the content alone,&#34; he said.</p><div class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Ever since Robinhood was founded in 2013, the firm has been at the center of the retail trading boom. </li>\n<li>Ahead of its IPO, Robinhood announced it is selling up to a third of its shares directly to retail investors. </li>\n<li>Insider asked six experts what to expect ahead of the popular trading app&#39;s stock market debut.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\"><strong>Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Robinhood&#39;s mission since it was founded in 2013 has been to &#34;democratize finance for all.&#34;</p><p>Years later, ahead of its hotly-anticipated initial public offering, founder Vlad Tenev is trying to make good on that promise by offering <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/robinhood-seeking-35-billion-ipo-2021-7\">a third</a> of the company&#39;s shares directly to customers through its app, a far greater amount than is usually offered to individual investors during most IPOs. </p><p>The decision was surprising, but gels with the company&#39;s stated mission to even the playing field between retail investors and massive institutions. Still, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/robinhood-ipo-risk-valuation-regulation-analysis-payment-order-flow-stock-2021-7\">some</a> experts have fretted over risks in the upcoming debut, particularly around the payment for order flow practice at the heart of Robinhood&#39;s business model.</p><p>Meanwhile, Robinhood itself has <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/robinhood-ipo-warns-meme-stock-status-day-trader-reddit-wallstreetbets-2021-7\">warned</a> investors that retail-trader interest could pose a risk to the stock price. </p><p>Still, Robinhood&#39;s IPO is among the most highly anticipated of the year. The company counts 17.7 million monthly active users, and the app added six million new active accounts in just the first quarter of this year. </p><p>The Menlo Park, California-based firm in its regulatory <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/0001783879/000162828021013986/robinhoods-1a1.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">filing</a> said it is aiming to raise as much as <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/robinhood-ipo-pricing-upcoming-stock-market-debut-offering-price-2021-7\">$2.3 billion</a> in its IPO. It is offering 55 million shares priced at $38-$42, putting its market valuation at <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/robinhood-ipo-pricing-upcoming-stock-market-debut-offering-price-2021-7\">$35 billion</a> at the top range. </p><p>According to reports, the company will start trading this coming Thursday, July 29, under the ticker HOOD. </p><p>Insider asked six experts on what to expect ahead of Robinhood&#39;s debut:</p><p><em>(Comments are lightly edited and condensed for clarity.)</em></p><h3>On reserving shares for retail investors</h3><p>&#34;I am struck by Robinhood&#39;s decision to reserve shares for their customers. This may be a strategy to try to build brand loyalty ... Many IPO processes allow participation restrictions that are somewhat skewed towards investors who are relatively informed about the business fundamentals.&#34; - <strong>Chester Spatt, finance professor at Carnegie Mellon University&#39;s Tepper School of Business. </strong></p><p>&#34;Robinhood is following the market trend of today&#39;s most innovative assets, such as bitcoin, by giving retail investors more or all of the first bite at the apple ahead of institutional investors. You no longer need to hit a certain level of financial eliteness in order to access portfolio-defining assets, and that is a meaningful win for retail investors.&#34; - <strong>Rodrigo Vicuna, CFO of Prime Trust.</strong></p><p>&#34;Selling almost a third of its offering directly to customers is a strategic decision by Robinhood to ensure they can keep a fixed customer base of retailers who use only Robinhood for trading. This will ensure that more retail investors buy the shares.&#34; - <strong>Ben Yankowitz, CFO of RocketFuel Blockchain, a payments processing firm</strong>.</p><h3><strong>On valuation</strong></h3><p><strong>&#34;</strong>With Robinhood&#39;s demographic and emotional connection with investors that have powered the rocket ship rides of AMC and Gamestop, anything is possible. The valuation is insane ... They are hoodwinking their clients. They tell people they aren&#39;t paying commissions but the commissions are just hidden in the trading.&#34; - <strong>Eric Schiffer, CEO of Patriarch Organization, a private equity firm.</strong></p><p>&#34;We can expect fireworks. Robinhood traders have become one of the biggest stories in finance over the past 12 months ... Robinhood seeking a valuation of around $35 billion strikes me as reasonable given this context ... I think it could have commanded a significantly higher valuation if it had not received so much negative press for the meme stock trade-halting controversy.&#34; - <strong>Josh Fraser, co-founder of Origin Protocol, a blockchain firm.</strong></p><p>&#34;Robinhood has seen tremendous success over the past 18 months ... I will say, however, that companies that IPO like this tend to see massive hype initially, followed by a sell-off, so if I was to invest in this, I would wait for that entry point rather than participate in the IPO.&#34; - <strong>Darren Franceschini, co-founder of BlockBank, an AI-powered banking platform.</strong></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 18:54:06","updatedTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","title":"The US economy's boom is far from over - even with the Delta surge","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-economy-will-be-fine-delta-covid-variant-case-surge-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fa06b00729770012b971e4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"shopping covid delta\" height=\"1665\" width=\"2220\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A person walks through a shopping district in Brooklyn on July 16, 2021 in New York City.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Spencer Platt/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>With the Delta variant surging, COVID worries on once again on the rise.</li>\n<li>But there&#39;s no reason to worry about the US economy, even with new restrictions being floated.</li>\n<li>A helpful Fed, the encouraging data around vaccines, and flush consumers should keep the economy chugging along.</li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Markets plunged earlier this week as concerns about the outlook swelled. The fear is in many ways understandable. COVID conditions, at least as proxied by cases, are deteriorating. At the same time, worrying economic trends have popped up in the form of a potentially more aggressive Federal Reserve and the market reflecting signs of weakening growth. </p><p>But just as stocks have mostly shrugged off their heartburn from earlier in the week, so too should you not get concerned about these developments. There&#39;s good reason to believe the US economy is going to hold up just fine.</p><h2><strong>The bad news</strong></h2><p>First, let&#39;s see why people are getting spooked.</p><p>First is the COVID story. In the US, hospitalizations are on the rise and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-coronavirus-deaths-surge-unvaccinated-long-term-effects-2021-7\">case positivity is at its highest rate</a> since April. Policymakers are even bringing up the possibility of renewed restrictions in some areas. In response, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/reopening-stocks-carnival-delta-stock-price-cruises-covid-delta-variant-2021-7\">reopening stocks got clipped</a>. Carnival Cruise Lines and Delta Airlines saw big drop offs early in the week and have sunk over the last few months. Planet Fitness is down while Peloton is up sharply. In other words, these companies are trading as if it is spring 2020 again and there is no effective vaccine. </p><p>Next, there are worries over the Fed&#39;s next meeting and whether the central bank is ready to take the foot off the gas when it comes to helping the economy. The market&#39;s current expectations for tapering - when the Fed will ease its support by slowing its buying of bonds - is for the process to begin sometime late this year, as recently reported by the WSJ. At any rate, it&#39;s odd to see the Fed tapering while concerns around COVID appear to be climbing.</p><p>Finally, growth concerns appear to be picking up. Corporate credit conditions, basically how affordable it is for companies to take on and pay back debt, are getting worse. This is a sign that investors don&#39;t think the booming pace of economic growth can keep up.</p><h2><strong>The good news</strong></h2><p>So, why don&#39;t I buy into the worries?</p><p>First, COVID is endemic. There is no doing away with it, but there is managing it. What I see shows that places that are vaccinated are not seeing a large increase in hospitalizations or deaths. The Delta variant originated in India, a population that does not have a large percent of its population vaccinated and cases there have declined quite sharply in recent weeks. In the UK, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/vaccinated-among-delta-deaths-but-older-relatively-few-uk-data-2021-6\">hospitalizations and deaths remain far below</a> where they were the last time cases were this high. So there is a good chance this wave ends up not being as devastating - in human or economic terms - as previous waves that have caused serious pain.</p><p>Moreover, it is not clear where the constituency is for new mitigation measures to slow the spread of the virus. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fully-vaccinated-people-not-immune-to-covid-milder-2021-7\">Vaccinated people are still relatively safe</a> from <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-vaccine-works-against-delta-covid-but-both-shots-needed-2021-7\">hospitalization and severe illness</a>, and unlikely to spread the virus in a material way. Unvaccinated people, by and large, do not want the mitigation measures in the first place. So despite saber rattling, political leaders might be reluctant to back off current reopening plans. The train has left the station.</p><p>Second, I do not think the Fed is going to abruptly shift policy and ease its support for the economy. New members of the Fed&#39;s interest rate setting committee are going to be even more unlikely to hike rates or taper off support in a serious way. The Fed has made it clear that they are willing to tolerate higher inflation to achieve its expansive goals on employment. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fb33a628e2cf0018905554?format=jpeg\" alt=\"capex\" height=\"778\" width=\"977\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Neil Dutta</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Finally, I don&#39;t see much downside to the economy. Consumers remain flush with cash and the spending boom continues. Inventories remain low and companies are likely to order plenty of new goods to stock their shelves in the months ahead, supporting manufacturing production. Homebuilders are working through backlogs, particularly now as construction costs have moderated, supporting residential investment. Capital spending intentions remain strong. </p><p>What does all this mean?</p><p>If I am right, then we should expect a sharp reversal of these moves in September. Dovish Fed plus stronger economy plus waning COVID equals back to risk on. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a it angered many retail investors</a> earlier this year when the trading app halted buying of GameStop, AMC, and other meme stocks amid an epic rally - and the company has pledged to earn back the href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/how-do-trading-apps-robinhood-webull-public-compare-brokerage-review-2021-5-1030476931?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" Monthly active users jumped by 6 million in the first three months of 2021 to 17.7 million from 11.7 million at the end of December, an increase of 51%.</p><p>The company on Saturday also outlined its plans to continue to grow revenue if US regulators ban <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/robinhood-payment-for-order-flow-gamestop-regulation-revenue-2021-2\">payment for order flow, at the heart of its business model.</a> Payment for order flow, or PFOF, is the practice of a brokerage receiving payment from a market maker to send customers&#39; shares to it. PFOF has drawn criticism from investor advocates who say it encourages brokerages to maximize their revenue at the expense of customers.</p><p>The company&#39;s chief financial officer, Jason Warnick, defended PFOF as &#34;a better deal for our customers versus the old commission structure.&#34;</p><p>&#34;That said, as we continue to add products and features to our platform we anticipate we will expand the sources of revenues we generate for the company,&#34; he added.</p><p>Robinhood said it plans to expand its securities lending business, invest more into Robinhood Gold, its subscription service, and expand internationally. It also said it&#39;s all-in on crypto. </p><p>Robinhood&#39;s IPO, planned for Thursday, is among the most <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/robinhood-ipo-risk-valuation-regulation-analysis-payment-order-flow-stock-2021-7?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">highly anticipated of the year</a>. During those talks, the companies &#34;agreed to multiple standstill agreements,&#34; but were unable to come to a solution, GM said.</p><p>&#34;Cruise and GM do not file this lawsuit lightly,&#34; counsel of medical professionals.\"</p>\n<p>Stephen Harmon, who was in his early 30s, was part of a Hillsong Church in California and a graduate of Hillsong College in Mesa, Arizona. Houston said on <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/CRnkbZ4MTsn/\">Instagram</a> Thursday Harmon had died from COVID-19.</p>\n<p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-variant-dont-lockdown-mask-mandates-covid-vaccine-passports-unvaccinated-2021-7\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Don't punish the vaccinated - make it harder to choose to be unvaccinated</a></em></p>\n<p>\"He was one of the most generous people I know and he had so much in front of him,\" Houston wrote.</p>\n<p>Hillsong Church, based in Australia, is a popular megachurch with celebrities such as Justin Bieber and Vanessa Hudgens. Recently, the church has been accused of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/after-bieber-pastor-carl-lentz-fired-hillsong-accused-of-discrimination-2020-12?r=hillsong-teaser\">racist and anti-LGBTQ behavior</a>.</p>\n<p>Prior to his death, Harmon had makes jokes online about the coronavirus and said he was not vaccinated, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/man-dies-of-covid-after-joking-about-vaccine-19-2021-7\">Insider's Ashley Collman</a> reported.</p>\n<p>In a June 3 tweet, he referenced Jay-Z's song \"99 Problems\" and wrote: \"If you're having email problems, I feel bad for you, son. I got 99 problems but a vax ain't one!\"</p>\n<p>On July 8, he again posted an anti-vaccine joke even after he was sick with COVID-19 and in an isolation ward, writing: \"And no, i will not be getting vaccinated once i am discharged and released.\"</p>\n<p>In his post about Harmon, Houston wrote, \"Stephen's thoughts on vaccines were his own.\"</p>\n<p>\"They do not represent the views and thoughts of Hillsong Church. Vlamis)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/60fcab6c17cf960019ee056c?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn8@2020_2/2021/07/25/10-54-24-364_1bb4820847f9a960.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn39@2020_3/2021/07/25/10-54-25-234_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=5991mjuHVRs:D4AzsH60N-M:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn80@2020_3/2021/07/25/10-54-24-372_60b5af8091bf84f7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=5991mjuHVRs:D4AzsH60N-M:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn51@2020_2/2021/07/25/10-54-23-206_ed13446f6c17a7ff.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn95@2020_6/2021/07/25/10-54-23-641_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=5991mjuHVRs:D4AzsH60N-M:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn87@2020_3/2021/07/25/10-54-24-364_17557d47f5798228.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/5991mjuHVRs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn19@2020_3/2021/07/25/10-54-22-137_0f22bacd55add1b6.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1627210446775},{"createdTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","updatedTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","title":"The performance of your stock portfolio can reflect the kind of music you listen to - with happy tunes correlating to higher returns, according to a top UK academic","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-returns-investor-emotions-music-choices-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60749bfa2cc1ef0018da1493?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Happy Stock Market Investor\" height=\"2012\" width=\"4024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Caroline Purser/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li aria-level=\"1\">What type of music people listen to is reflected in stock markets, Finance professor Alex Edmans says.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">There is a correlation between the positivity of music and returns, volatility, fund flows and even government bonds.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">This is because emotions drive decision making and are reflected in music choices, Edmans argues.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\"><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestts&#38;utm_medium=ingest\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>What type of songs you listen to could be reflected in how your stock portfolio performs, as there is evidence of a correlation between the positivity of the music investors listen to and returns, according to Alex Edmans, who is professor of finance at London Business School.</p><p>Traditional economic belief is that fundamentals impact markets - but humans aren&#39;t automated robots, Edmans told Insider in an interview. Their mood impacts their decision making, and this extends too to their investment decisions that ultimately impact markets. </p><p>The base assumption for Edmans&#39; research is that people&#39;s happiness levels are often reflected in what songs they listen to and therefore music choices and market developments can be linked to one another. </p><p>&#34;In weeks in which the citizens of a country are listening to more happy music, the market goes up and in weeks in which they are listening to unhappy music the market goes down. So the music you&#39;re listening to is linked to stock returns,&#34; he explained to Insider in an interview. </p><p>The research is based on data from Spotify, one of the biggest music streaming platforms. It tracks what songs are being played in different countries, as well as assigning them a positivity or negativity score. The researchers used this as one metric to measure the mood of populations before linking it to market events.</p><p>And it is not just stock market returns that can be correlated with music choices. Volatility for example is also mirrored in music - the more people play extremely positive or extremely negative songs, the more market volatility rises, Edmans&#39; research found. </p><p>When it comes to net equity fund flows, more positive music choices can be associated with higher inflows. And looking at government bonds, an increase in negative, or sad songs, being played can be correlated with investors buying into bonds. This is in line with the idea of investors moving into safer assets during periods of low market expectations, he said.</p><p>The research could have real-life implications for investors as it provides evidence for a link between someone&#39;s mood and their investment choices, Edmans said. </p><p>&#34;By showing that emotions actually drive stock returns, that&#39;s just highlighting the importance of traders just being very aware and careful of their emotions and not to trade, perhaps, when they&#39;re in an extremely good mood or an extremely bad mood,&#34; he said. </p><p>&#34;One thing that a lot of other research actually suggests is that when people trade, the average trade loses money. [... ] And what we&#39;re suggesting in this paper is one of the reasons might be that these trades are driven by emotions rather than fundamentals.&#34;</p><p>This does not just apply to professional investors - retail crypto traders for example are just as driven by emotions, Edmans believes. And this can make their investments riskier and losses more likely, he said.  </p><p>Whether you are a professional or retail investor, caution around emotion is therefore key, he said. </p><p>&#34;What we&#39;re saying is just hold your horses sometimes before making a trading decision and to make sure that what really is driving it is analysis rather than emotion,&#34; Edmans said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-returns-investor-emotions-music-choices-2021-7'>Business Insider</a></div><div more inviting to all types of women, Victoria&#39;s Secret is giving a makeover to its brick-and-mortar stores, trading the signature bubblegum pink decor and the six-foot, rail-thin mannequins for a modern blush pink and fuller-figured displays.</p><p>I got the chance to visit one of the newly revamped stores at the Polaris Fashion Place shopping mall, near the company&#39;s Columbus, Ohio, headquarters.</p><p>While I noticed plenty of new and welcome changes during my visit, I left still feeling like Victoria&#39;s Secret is peddling a version of womanhood that&#39;s unattainable to lots of women - myself included. </p><h2>Seeing curvier mannequins at the entrance made me hopeful the rebrand would be inclusive of plus-size women and girls.</h2><figure>\n\t<img class=\"copyright\">Mandy Shunnarah</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In fact, the first thing I noticed when I entered the store was that I didn&#39;t immediately hate myself. I turned 12 in 2002, right as the Victoria&#39;s Secret PINK line for teenagers was launched. Through high school and college, as I rocked VS-branded underthings in every color, it never occurred to me that one day I wouldn&#39;t fit into Victoria&#39;s Secret panties - perhaps because I was too busy starving myself in hopes of looking like the angel wing- and lingerie-clad models whose pictures hung throughout the store I shopped at.</p><p>And when I recovered from my eating disorder by gaining 60 pounds, I found that even their stretchiest XXL panties - the largest size VS makes - dug uncomfortably into my hips. </p><h2><strong>So it was a welcome change to see full-figured mannequins, some as short as five feet, placed throughout the store.</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fac4200729770012b97d99?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Victoria&#39;s Secret src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fac5ff0729770012b97ec9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mandy Shunnarah\" height=\"2643\" width=\"3525\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mandy Shunnarah</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Instead of photos of Angels on display, there were photos of models living life, happy and confident. For example, near the sports bras were photos of models carrying surfboards and wearing athleisure; neither of them appeared to worry about looking sexy. </p><p>For a company that&#39;s been woefully slow to change, these are much needed steps in the right direction.</p><h2>However, upon closer inspection, I realized that &#39;full-figured&#39; mannequin didn&#39;t mean plus-sized. </h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fac47d0729770012b97dd2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Victoria&#39;s Secret rebrand columbus ohio Mandy Shunnarah\" height=\"2932\" width=\"3909\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mandy Shunnarah</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Even with full-figured mannequins mixed in, several displays still featured exclusively slim mannequins. And when I checked what size panty a full-figured mannequin wore, I found it was an XL.</p><h2><strong>Victoria&#39;s Secret CEO Martin Waters said on a recent earnings call that the rebrand is about &#39;including all women.&#39;</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fac53efc2536001820064f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Victoria&#39;s Secret rebrand columbus ohio Mandy Shunnarah\" height=\"3042\" width=\"4057\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mandy Shunnarah</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><a href=\"https://nypost.com/2021/07/18/victorias-secret-scrubs-the-angels-from-its-stores-in-revamp/\">Walters said</a> it&#39;s about &#34;going from a look to a feeling, from excluding most women to including all women, from mostly unattainable to grounded in real life.&#34;</p><p>And while Victoria&#39;s Secret has embraced models of color and sells nude undergarments in several skin tones, the brand has not yet embraced plus-size women in the same way.</p><h2>Full-figured mannequins may have greeted you at the entrance, but once inside the store, some displays appeared much like they have in the past.</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fac6cc0729770012b97f40?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mandy Shunnarah\" height=\"2388\" width=\"3184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mandy Shunnarah</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>I&#39;m a size 14, the same size as Victoria&#39;s Secret&#39;s plus-size model du jour, Paloma Elsesser. A size 14 was once thought to be the average size of American women until a <a href=\"https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/abs/10.1080/17543266.2016.1214291?journalCode=tfdt20\">2017 study</a> found that the average American woman &#34;wears between a misses size 16 to 18, which corresponds to a women&#39;s plus-size 20W.&#34; </p><h2><strong>I couldn&#39;t help but wonder how the brand can achieve the goal of &#39;including all women&#39; without expanding its limited sizing.</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fac739fc2536001820077c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mandy Shunnarah VS Victoria&#39;s Secret\" height=\"2643\" width=\"3525\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mandy Shunnarah</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>If I&#39;m a size 14, which is on the smaller end of the plus-size range, and the largest panties Victoria&#39;s Secret makes are uncomfortably tight on me, I think about the 50% or more of women who are still unable to wear the brand. </p><h2>Even with the updates, many of the displays look largely the same to me.</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fac91b0729770012b980df?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mandy Shunnarah Victoria&#39;s Secret\" height=\"2424\" width=\"3233\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mandy Shunnarah</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>When shoppers have criticized the brand, I don&#39;t believe they were asking for new wall colors and different furniture;  they were asking for inclusivity, including expanded sizing.</p><p>After all, by including full-figured mannequins, it wasn&#39;t as though those with thigh gaps had all been replaced - there were just curvier mannequins placed alongside them. I&#39;m still larger than every single mannequin in the store. </p><h2><strong>For much of its history, Victoria&#39;s Secret has sold an aspirational ideal of femininity.</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fac9500729770012b98105?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mandy Shunnarah Victoria&#39;s Secret\" height=\"2397\" width=\"3197\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mandy Shunnarah</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Even with the new VS Collective of models chosen for their accomplishments - a group that includes Megan Rapinoe, Priyanka Chopra Jonas, and Amanda de Cadenet, among others - the store rebrand without sizing expansion still feels like they&#39;re peddling a version of womanhood that&#39;s still unattainable to me. </p><h2><strong>The decor updates are aesthetically pleasing, but at the end of the day, I still can&#39;t buy VS panties.</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fac7a50729770012b98005?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mandy Shunnarah Victoria&#39;s Secret\" height=\"2643\" width=\"3525\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mandy Shunnarah</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The store still feels familiar and like overall little has changed. In short, the updates feel like the bare minimum the brand could do to garner goodwill among its customer base. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 91b0729770012b980df?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn43@2020_2/2021/07/25/10-54-21-733_2d9ef0fe2e93b183.webp","https://i.insider.com/60fac9500729770012b98105?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn63@2020_4/2021/07/25/10-54-25-342_862ee2379822adeb.webp","https://i.insider.com/60fac7a50729770012b98005?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn15@2020_6/2021/07/25/10-54-24-430_7feed3b7750d83ac.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn39@2020_3/2021/07/25/10-54-25-234_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=cZtWPNPb280:Vwe6O43InaY:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn12@2020_3/2021/07/25/10-54-23-329_b1e6aee54d90e136.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=cZtWPNPb280:Vwe6O43InaY:V_sGLiPBpWU":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn95@2020_6/2021/07/25/10-54-23-641_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=cZtWPNPb280:Vwe6O43InaY:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn8@2020_4/2021/07/25/10-54-23-350_9695ed089cd85a73.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/cZtWPNPb280":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn64@2020_1/2021/07/25/10-54-22-836_c5a709a417e04d7e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1627210446761},{"createdTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","updatedTime":"2021-07-25 18:54:06","title":"The week the Delta variant threatened the economy","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-covid-variant-cases-threatening-economy-markets-reopening-lockdown-02021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fb139f0729770012b9ab9f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"vaccine covid\" height=\"1600\" width=\"2133\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Delta variant of the coronavirus is putting the unvaccinated at risk.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Irfan Khan/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-variant-new-covid-19-cases-cdc-director-2021-7\">highly contagious Delta variant</a> of the coronavirus now makes up the majority of US Covid cases.</li>\n<li>Americans are getting worried, sending markets on a <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-news-today-dow-falls-delta-variant-covid-economy-2021-7\">fleeting plunge</a> this week.</li>\n<li>While economic data suggests a robust recovery, the Delta variant remains a threat. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Just when Americans are getting into the throes of a <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/hot-vaxx-summer-pandemic-horniness-is-coming-blissful-release-2021-3\">hot vaxx summer</a>, the Delta variant of the coronavirus is trying to stop the fun.</p><p>The far more contagious variant currently accounts for 83% of all new sequenced COVID-19 cases in the US, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-variant-new-covid-19-cases-cdc-director-2021-7\">the CDC announced on Monday</a>. That&#39;s up from 50% the week of July 3, and even higher in <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-coronavirus-variant-hitting-republican-states-vaccine-divide-2021-7\">areas of the US with low vaccination rates</a>, CDC Director Rochelle Walensky said. </p><p>She added that America is entering a &#34;pandemic of the unvaccinated&#34;</p><p>It&#39;s increased the odds of Covid &#34;breakthrough&#34; infections among vaccinated people, a growing minority of which - from the New York <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/all-3-yankees-who-tested-positive-for-covid-19-vaccinated-2021-7\">Yankees</a> to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-vaccine-breakthrough-infection-delta-variant-fully-vaccinated-las-vegas-2021-7\">Vegas partygoers</a> - have caught Covid. The good news is that the vaccinated <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fully-vaccinated-people-not-immune-to-covid-milder-2021-7https://www.businessinsider.com/fully-vaccinated-people-not-immune-to-covid-milder-2021-7\">remain well protected</a> from serious disease, likely to have mild or no symptoms, and carrying with them a low transmission risk. </p><p>But Biden officials and the CDC are reportedly <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-administration-considers-stricter-mask-guidance-as-delta-variant-spreads-2021-7\">considering stricter mask-wearing guidance</a> to protect unvaccinated people as Delta cases spike. Dr. Anthony Fauci has even said that fully vaccinated Americans <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-variant-vaccine-fully-vaccinated-face-mask-fauci-indoor-cdc-2021-7\">may &#34;want to consider&#34;</a> wearing masks indoors again.</p><p>It doesn&#39;t help that <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/everyone-has-a-cold-now-masks-off-old-viruses-circulating-2021-7\">the common cold is running rampant</a> across the US as we return to socializing with others sans masks. Respiratory viruses, which mimic Covid-like symptoms, are giving many a Covid scare.</p><p>With only half the population vaccinated, all the germs on the loose were enough to put America on edge this week. </p><h2><strong>A threat to the economy</strong></h2><p>As fears over the Delta variant have risen, even Fox News began emphasizing vaccine awareness and the efficacy of vaccines. The network&#39;s vaccine coverage has often mirrored its overall pandemic framing of public health measures as culture wars, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-fox-news-changed-its-stance-on-vaccines-hannity-tucker-2021-7\">Insider&#39;s Jake Lahut reported</a>.</p><p>While several hosts have previously touted the shots, Monday saw a significant leap in the network&#39;s vaccine promotion. Fox News hosts cranked up their vaccine messaging and programming featured banners of the federal government&#39;s vaccine domain page.</p><p>Markets freaked out on the same day, with the S&#38;P 500 closing down about 1.6% on the day. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-news-today-dow-falls-delta-variant-covid-economy-2021-7\">Investors appeared to be spooked</a> about the rise in Delta variant cases across the country. That worry was fleeting, however, as stocks quickly rebounded over the next couple days, with the S&#38;P 500 closing higher on Thursday than it had the week before. Stocks <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-news-today-sp-500-nasdaq-close-records-earnings-2021-7\">even ended the week hitting record highs</a>.</p><div class=\"insider-raw-embed\"><iframe title=\"S&#38;P 500 500\" aria-label=\"Interactive line chart\" id=\"datawrapper-chart-bAKaZ\" src=\"https://datawrapper.dwcdn.net/bAKaZ/1/\" scrolling=\"no\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"width: 0; min-width: 100% ; border: none;\" height=\"450\"></iframe><script type=\"text/javascript\">!function(){&#34;use strict&#34;;window.addEventListener(&#34;message&#34;,(function(e){if(void 0!==e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;]){var t=document.querySelectorAll(&#34;iframe&#34;);for(var a in e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;])for(var r=0;r&#60;t.length;r++){if(t[r].contentWindow===e.source)t[r].style.height=e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;][a]+&#34;px&#34;}}}))}();\n</script></div><p>Still, the presence of the Delta threat is real. The US <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-july-4-independence-from-virus-celebration-vaccination-goal-missed-2021-6\">missed President Joe Biden&#39;s goal</a> to have at least 70% of adults partially vaccinated by July 4. Currently, <a href=\"https://covid.cdc.gov/covid-data-tracker/#vaccinations\">68.6% of adults</a> are partially vaccinated and only 59% fully vaccinated. </p><p>That leaves millions unvaccinated, at risk of exposure to the variant. Left unchecked, it could slow down America&#39;s economic recovery. </p><p>A new round of shutdowns or unimpeded spread of the highly contagious Delta variant among the unvaccinated population could lead to businesses closing and more layoffs and furloughs like what was seen last spring. It could also make the American shopper <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-variant-covid-economy-consumer-behavior-lockdown-bank-of-america-2021-7\">go back into lockdown</a>, Bank of America forecasted. And, while the CDC has urged schools to fully reopen, there&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.khon2.com/local-news/rise-in-coronavirus-cases-ahead-of-new-school-year-leaves-uncertainty-about-return-to-campus/\">still uncertainty around returning</a> as coronavirus cases rise again. </p><p>But this hasn&#39;t happened yet, and most of the economic data from the last several weeks still suggests a robust recovery. The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/june-jobs-report-850000-payrolls-unemployment-rate-labor-market-shortage-2021-7\">US added 850,000 jobs in June</a>, getting the labor market steadily closer to recovering the jobs lost in spring 2020. The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/leisure-hospitality-june-jobs-report-wages-increased-labor-force-2021-7\">leisure and hospitality sector</a> in particular, which includes restaurants, bars, and hotels that were hit especially hard last spring, saw rapid job growth and big wage gains for workers.</p><p>Economists expect <a href=\"https://www.investing.com/economic-calendar/gdp-375?utm_source=WMT_EC&utm_medium=Referral&utm_campaign=COMaign=COM\">next week&#39;s gross domestic product</a> figures to show the US economy expanding at the fastest pace since the early 1980s, with the exception of a spike last fall coming off the historically low levels of activity last spring.</p><p>Still, the Delta virus is <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2021/06/17/delta-variant-global-concern/\">adding a speed bump</a> in America&#39;s path to a post-pandemic world. While we may be progressing toward normalcy, life still won&#39;t be completely normal by fall. The economy is still under threat.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fcc28717cf960019ee05ad?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Asa Hutchinson\" height=\"3478\" width=\"4638\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption>\n   Arkansas Gov. Asa Hutchinson speaks at a news conference at the Arkansas state Capitol in Little Rock, Ark., Tuesday, Aug. 4, 2015. \n   <p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Danny Johnston</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\"> \n <li>Arkansas is among the states seeing a surge in COVID-19 cases, as many residents are unvaccinated.</li> \n <li>Republican Gov. Asa Hutchinson said it's \"disappointing\" that vaccines have become \"political.\"</li> \n <li>He's been traveling throughout the state to combat hesitancy and encourage people to get the shot.</li> \n <li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider's business page</a>.</li> \n</ul>\n<p>Arkansas Gov. Asa Hutchinson said Thursday it's \"disappointing\" vaccines have become \"political,\" as his state deals with a COVID-19 surge.</p>\n<p>Hutchinson, a Republican, was speaking to Greta Van Susteren on her show \"<a href=\"https://www.fullcourtgreta.com/video/2021/07/25/overtime-gov-hutchinson-says-arkansas-economy-is-strong-despite-covid/\">Full Court Press</a>\" when the host asked him about the state's low vaccination rate.</p>\n<p>\"That's a big challenge for us,\" Hutchinson said, noting that there is lots of vaccine resistance. \"It's a conservative state. Sometimes conservatives are hesitant about the government. And we just got to counteract that by getting better information to them, building confidence.\"</p>\n<p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-variant-dont-lockdown-mask-mandates-covid-vaccine-passports-unvaccinated-2021-7\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Don't punish the vaccinated - make it harder to choose to be unvaccinated</a></em></p>\n<p>In Arkansas, 44.8% of the state's population has been fully vaccinated, while 52.1% has received at least one dose. That leaves the state with one of the lowest vaccination rates per capita. Only Alabama and Mississippi have a smaller percentage of fully vaccinated residents, according to CDC data compiled by the <a href=\"https://www.mayoclinic.org/coronavirus-covid-19/vaccine-tracker\">Mayo Clinic</a>.</p>\n<p>Susteren asked Hutchinson about how vaccine hesitancy happens along political lines.</p>\n<p>\"It is disappointing that there's a political part to this,\" he said.</p>\n<p>Vaccine hesitancy has been especially prominent among Republicans and in <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2021/04/17/us/vaccine-hesitancy-politics.html\">counties</a> that voted for former President Donald Trump.</p>\n<p>But Hutchinson said he both supported Trump and got the vaccine, and noted that Trump himself is also vaccinated. He also said that in Arkansas, where more than 65% of the vote went to Trump, tens of thousands of people had already gotten the vaccine.</p>\n<p>Arkansas is among the states seeing a <a href=\"https://www.kark.com/news/health/coronavirus/covid-19-in-arkansas-active-cases-surge-past-15000-more-than-2000-new-cases-in-24-hours/\">surge</a> in COVID-19 cases as the Delta variant rapidly spreads. Hutchinson has been traveling around the state to address vaccine hesitancy and encourage people to get vaccinated, <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2021/07/19/1018025449/arkansas-governor-hits-the-road-to-combat-vaccine-hesitancy\">NPR</a> reported.</p>\n<p><em>Have a news tip?
